Topic: Math
Question: A computer routine was developed to generate two numbers (x,y) the first being a random number between 0 and 100 inclusive, and the second being less than or equal to the square root of the first. Each of the following pair satisfies the routine except
Choices:
  A: (99,10)
  B: (85,9)
  C: (50,7)
  D: (1,1)
  E: (1,0)
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  - The first number (x) is a random number between 0 and 100 inclusive.
  - The second number (y) is less than or equal to the square root of the first number (x).
  - To satisfy the routine, the second number (y) must be less than or equal to the square root of the first number (x).
  
Checking each option:
  A: (99,10) satisfies the routine because 10 is less than or equal to the square root of 99.
  B: (85,9) satisfies the routine because 9 is less than or equal to the square root of 85.
  C: (50,7) satisfies the routine because 7 is less than or equal to the square root of 50.
  D: (1,1) satisfies the routine because 1 is less than or equal to the square root of 1.
  E: (1,0) does not satisfy the routine because 0 is not less than or equal to the square root of 1.

Action: Answer("E")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  - The first number (x) is a random number between 0 and 100 inclusive.
  - The second number (y) is less than or equal to the square root of the first number (x).
  - To check if a pair satisfies the routine, we need to verify that the second number (y) is less than or equal to the square root of the first number (x).
  
Checking each pair:
  - For pair (99,10), 10 <= sqrt(99) is true.
  - For pair (85,9), 9 <= sqrt(85) is true.
  - For pair (50,7), 7 <= sqrt(50) is true.
  - For pair (1,1), 1 <= sqrt(1) is true.
  - For pair (1,0), 0 <= sqrt(1) is true.
  
All pairs satisfy the routine, so the answer is None of the Above.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 1.0 | Problem 2 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: If 75 percent of the employees of a certain company take a winter vacation, 40 percent take a winter and a summer vacation, and 20 percent take neither a winter nor a summer vacation, what Q percent of the employees take a summer vacation but not a winter vacation?
Choices:
  A: 5%
  B: 15%
  C: 25%
  D: 35%
  E: 45%
Response 0:
Let's assume that there are 100 employees in the company. 

Knowledge:
- 75% of the employees take a winter vacation, which means 75 employees take a winter vacation.
- 40% of the employees take a winter and a summer vacation, which means 40 employees take both vacations.
- 20% of the employees take neither a winter nor a summer vacation, which means 20 employees take neither vacation.
- We want to find the percentage of employees who take a summer vacation but not a winter vacation.

To find the percentage of employees who take a summer vacation but not a winter vacation, we need to subtract the number of employees who take both vacations from the number of employees who take only a summer vacation.

The number of employees who take only a summer vacation can be found by subtracting the number of employees who take both vacations from the number of employees who take a summer vacation:
Summer vacation only = Total summer vacation - Both vacations
Summer vacation only = (100-Q)% - 40%

Now, we can substitute the given values and solve for Q:
75% of 100 = 75 employees take a winter vacation
40% of 100 = 40 employees take both vacations
20% of 100 = 20 employees take neither vacation
Thus, 15% of 100 = 100% - 75% - 20% = 5% of employees take only a winter vacation
Summer vacation only = (100-Q)% - 40%
20% = (100-Q)% - 40%
60% = (100-Q)%
Q = 40%

Answer: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Let's assume that there are 100 employees in the company. 

Knowledge:
- 75% of the employees take a winter vacation, which means 75 employees take a winter vacation.
- 40% of the employees take a winter and a summer vacation, which means 40 employees take both vacations.
- 20% of the employees take neither a winter nor a summer vacation, which means 20 employees take neither vacation.
- We want to find the percentage of employees who take a summer vacation but not a winter vacation.

To find the percentage of employees who take a summer vacation but not a winter vacation, we need to subtract the number of employees who take both vacations from the number of employees who take only a summer vacation.

The number of employees who take only a summer vacation can be found by subtracting the number of employees who take both vacations from the number of employees who take a summer vacation:
Summer vacation only = Total summer vacation - Both vacations
Summer vacation only = (100-Q)% - 40%

We know that 20% of the employees take neither vacation, so the percentage of employees who take at least one vacation is:
100% - 20% = 80%

We also know that 75% of the employees take a winter vacation, and 40% take both vacations. This means that the percentage of employees who take a summer vacation is:
80% - 75% + 40% = 45%

Now we can substitute the value of the percentage of employees who take a summer vacation into the equation we derived earlier:
Summer vacation only = (100-Q)% - 40%
Summer vacation only = 45% - 40%
Summer vacation only = 5%

Action: Answer("A")

Calculation:
Let's assume that Q percent of the employees take a summer vacation but not a winter vacation.
The number of employees who take a summer vacation is (100-Q)%.
The number of employees who take both vacations is 40%.
The number of employees who take only a winter vacation is (75-40)% = 35%.
The number of employees who take neither vacation is 20%.
So, the number of employees who take only a summer vacation is:
(100-Q)% - 40% - 35% - 20% = 5% - Q%
We know that this number is positive, so:
5% - Q% > 0
Q% < 5%

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 1.0 | Problem 3 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A rectangular solid, 3 x 4 x 15, is inscribed in a sphere, so that all eight of its vertices are on the sphere. What is the diameter of the sphere?
Choices:
  A:  13.3542
  B:  15.8113
  C:  18.3451
  D:  19.5667
  E:  20.8888
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  A rectangular solid has 8 vertices.
  The diameter of a sphere is twice the radius of the sphere.
  The radius of the sphere is the distance from the center of the sphere to any point on the sphere.
  The longest diagonal of the rectangular solid is the diameter of the sphere.
  The longest diagonal of a rectangular solid with sides a, b, and c is given by the formula sqrt(a^2 + b^2 + c^2).
  In this case, a = 3, b = 4, and c = 15.
Action: Answer("D")  
Solution:
  The longest diagonal of the rectangular solid is sqrt(3^2 + 4^2 + 15^2) = sqrt(250).
  The diameter of the sphere is equal to the longest diagonal of the rectangular solid, so the diameter is 2*sqrt(250) = 19.5667 (rounded to four decimal places).
  Therefore, the answer is D: 19.5667.
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  A rectangular solid is a 3D shape with six faces, all of which are rectangles.
  The length, width, and height of the rectangular solid are 3, 4, and 15, respectively.
  The diameter of a sphere is twice the length of its radius.
  The radius of the sphere is equal to the distance from the center of the sphere to any of its vertices.
  The distance from the center of the sphere to any of the vertices of the rectangular solid is equal to half of the diagonal of the rectangular solid.
  The diagonal of the rectangular solid can be found using the Pythagorean theorem.
  The Pythagorean theorem states that for a right triangle with legs a and b and hypotenuse c, a^2 + b^2 = c^2.
  Therefore, the diagonal of the rectangular solid is sqrt(3^2 + 4^2 + 15^2) = sqrt(250) = 5*sqrt(10).
  The radius of the sphere is half of the diagonal of the rectangular solid, which is 5*sqrt(10)/2 = (5/2)*sqrt(10).
  The diameter of the sphere is twice the radius, which is 5*sqrt(10).
Action: Answer("E")
Response 2:
Knowledge:
  A rectangular solid has 8 vertices.
  The diameter of a sphere is twice the radius of the sphere.
  The radius of the sphere is the distance from the center of the sphere to any point on the sphere.
  The longest diagonal of the rectangular solid is the diameter of the sphere.
  The longest diagonal of a rectangular solid can be found using the Pythagorean theorem.
  The Pythagorean theorem states that for a right triangle with legs of length a and b and hypotenuse of length c, a^2 + b^2 = c^2.
  The longest diagonal of the rectangular solid can be found by applying the Pythagorean theorem twice.
  The longest diagonal of the rectangular solid is sqrt(3^2 + 4^2 + 15^2) = sqrt(250).
  The diameter of the sphere is twice the radius of the sphere, which is equal to half the length of the longest diagonal of the rectangular solid.
  Therefore, the diameter of the sphere is 2 * sqrt(250) / 2 = sqrt(250).

  B: 39 seconds
  C: 20 seconds
  D: 33 seconds

  - The train's speed is 120 miles per hour.
  - We can use the formula: time = distance / speed
  
Calculation:
  - The train needs to travel 1 mile to pass completely through the tunnel.
  - Using the formula, time = distance / speed = 1 mile / 120 miles per hour = 1/120 hours.
  - We need to convert hours to seconds: 1/120 hours * 3600 seconds/hour = 30 seconds.
  - The train takes 3 seconds to enter and 3 seconds to exit, so the total time to pass completely through the tunnel is 30 + 3 + 3 = 36 seconds.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 1.0 | Problem 7 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A bookshelf contains 45 books, 30 of which are hardcover and 20 of which are fiction. What is the maximum number of books that are both hardcover and fiction?
Choices:
  A: 10
  B: 15
  C: 18
  D: 20
  E: 30
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  We can use the formula: Total = Group1 + Group2 - Both + Neither
  We are given:
    Total number of books = 45
    Number of hardcover books = 30
    Number of fiction books = 20
    We want to find the maximum number of books that are both hardcover and fiction.
  We can use the formula to solve for the maximum number of books that are both hardcover and fiction:
    45 = 30 + 20 - Both + Neither
    Simplifying the equation, we get:
    Both - Neither = 5
    Since we want to find the maximum number of books that are both hardcover and fiction, we want to maximize the value of Both.
    The maximum value of Both will occur when the value of Neither is minimized.
    The minimum value of Neither is 0, which means that all 20 fiction books are hardcover.
Action: Answer("B") 
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  We can use the formula: Total = Group1 + Group2 - Both + Neither
  We know that Total = 45, Group1 (hardcover) = 30, and Group2 (fiction) = 20.
  We want to find the maximum number of books that are both hardcover and fiction, which is Both.
  We can use the formula to solve for Both: Both = Group1 + Group2 - Total + Neither
  We want to find the maximum value of Both, which means we want to find the minimum value of Neither.
  The minimum value of Neither occurs when all the remaining books are not hardcover and not fiction.
  Therefore, Neither = Total - (Group1 + Group2) = 45 - (30 + 20) = 45 - 50 = -5.
  However, we cannot have a negative number of books, so the minimum value of Neither is 0.
  Therefore, Both = Group1 + Group2 - Total + Neither = 30 + 20 - 45 + 0 = 5.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 2:
Knowledge:
  We can use the formula: Total = Group1 + Group2 - Both + Neither
  Total: Total number of books in the bookshelf (45)
  Group1: Number of hardcover books (30)
  Group2: Number of fiction books (20)
  Both: Number of books that are both hardcover and fiction (unknown)
  Neither: Number of books that are neither hardcover nor fiction (unknown)
  We can solve for Both by rearranging the formula: Both = Group1 + Group2 - Total + Neither
  We know that Neither must be a non-negative number, since it is impossible to have negative books.

Question: An electric pole, 14 metres high, casts a shadow of 10 metres. Find the height of a tree that casts a shadow of 15 metres under similar conditions.
Choices:
  A: 21
  B: 22
  C: 20
  D: 23
  E: 24
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  If two objects are similar, then their corresponding sides are proportional.
  Let h be the height of the tree and x be the length of its shadow.
  We can set up a proportion: h/15 = 14/10
  Solving for h, we get h = 21.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  The height of an object and its shadow are proportional to the height and shadow of another object under similar conditions.
  We can use the formula: height of object / length of shadow = height of another object / length of its shadow

Action: 
  Let x be the height of the tree.
  Using the formula, we have:
  14 / 10 = x / 15
  Solving for x, we get:
  x = 21
  Therefore, the height of the tree is 21 meters.

Topic: Math
Question: At what price should the Karan mark a sewing machine that costs him Rs. 1200/- so that even after offering a 20% discount, he makes 20% profit?
Choices:
  A: 1,879
  B: 1,875
  C: 1,876
  D: 1,872
  E: 1,800
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Let the marked price be M.
  Cost price of the sewing machine is Rs. 1200.
  Karan wants to make a 20% profit even after offering a 20% discount.
  Profit percentage = (Profit / Cost Price) * 100
  Selling Price = M - (20% of M)
  A: Calculation is incorrect.
  B: Calculation is incorrect.
  C: Calculation is correct.
  D: Calculation is incorrect.
  E: Calculation is incorrect.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Let the marked price be M.
  Cost price of the sewing machine is Rs. 1200.
  Karan wants to make a profit of 20%.
  Karan offers a discount of 20%.
  Selling price = Marked price - Discount
  Profit = Selling price - Cost price
  
Calculation:
  Let's first calculate the selling price after discount.
  Selling price = Marked price - Discount
  Discount = 20% of Marked price = 0.2M
  Selling price = M - 0.2M = 0.8M
  
  Now, let's calculate the profit.
  Profit = Selling price - Cost price
  Profit = 0.8M - 1200
  
  Karan wants to make a profit of 20%.
  Profit = 20% of Cost price = 0.2 * 1200 = 240
  
  Therefore, 0.8M - 1200 = 240
  0.8M = 1440
  M = 1800
  
Action: Answer("E")
Response 2:

  The profit percentage is (Selling Price - Cost Price)/Cost Price * 100%

  Let's calculate the selling price first.
  Selling Price = (1-20/100)*M = 0.8M
  Profit Percentage = (Selling Price - Cost Price)/Cost Price * 100%

  20 = (0.8M/1200) * 100

  B: 2,020
  C: 2,100
  D: 2,200
  E: 1,900

  We can choose the middle letter in 5 ways.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 1.0 | Problem 11 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: At a certain factory, 10 percent of the staplers produced on Monday were defective and 2 percent of the non-defective staplers were rejected by mistake. If 72 of the non-defective staplers were rejected, what was the number of staplers produced that day?
Choices:
  A: 4,000
  B: 4,200
  C: 4,500
  D: 4,800
  E: 5,000
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Let's assume that the total number of staplers produced on Monday is "x".
  10 percent of the staplers produced on Monday were defective, so the number of defective staplers is 0.1x.
  The remaining staplers are non-defective, so the number of non-defective staplers is 0.9x.
  2 percent of the non-defective staplers were rejected by mistake, so the number of rejected non-defective staplers is 0.02 * 0.9x = 0.018x.
  We know that 72 of the non-defective staplers were rejected, so 0.018x = 72.
  Solving for x, we get x = 4000.
Action: Answer("A")

  Solving for x, we get x = 4000.

  B: MD/3
  C: M/(D-3)
  D: 3D/(M2-3M)
  E: None of these

  Therefore, the new amount that each man has to contribute will be (D/(M-3)).

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 1.0 | Problem 15 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: The events A and B are independent. The probability that event A occurs is 0.6, and the probability that at least one of the events A or B occurs is 0.96. What is the probability that event B occurs?
Choices:
  A: 0.5
  B: 0.6
  C: 0.7
  D: 0.8
  E: 0.9
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  If events A and B are independent, then the probability of both events occurring is the product of their individual probabilities: P(A and B) = P(A) * P(B).
  The probability of at least one of two events occurring is the sum of their individual probabilities minus the probability of both events occurring: P(A or B) = P(A) + P(B) - P(A and B).
  We are given that P(A) = 0.6 and P(A or B) = 0.96.

Solution:
  We can use the formula for P(A or B) to find P(B):
  P(A or B) = P(A) + P(B) - P(A and B)
  0.96 = 0.6 + P(B) - (0.6 * P(B))  (substituting the given values)
  0.96 = 0.6 + 0.4P(B)
  0.36 = 0.4P(B)
  P(B) = 0.36 / 0.4
  P(B) = 0.9

Action: Answer("E")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  If events A and B are independent, then the probability of both events occurring is the product of their individual probabilities: P(A and B) = P(A) * P(B).
  The probability of at least one of the events A or B occurring is the sum of their individual probabilities minus the probability of both events occurring: P(A or B) = P(A) + P(B) - P(A and B).
  We can use the formula P(A or B) = P(A) + P(B) - P(A and B) to solve for P(B).
  
Solution:
  Let P(B) = x.
  We know that P(A) = 0.6 and P(A or B) = 0.96.
  P(A or B) = P(A) + P(B) - P(A and B)
  0.96 = 0.6 + x - (0.6 * x)  [substituting the given values]
  0.96 = 0.6 + x - 0.6x
  0.96 = 0.6 + 0.4x
  0.36 = 0.4x
  x = 0.9
  
Action: Answer("E")
Response 2:
Knowledge:
  If events A and B are independent, then the probability of both events occurring is the product of their individual probabilities: P(A and B) = P(A) * P(B).
  The probability of at least one of two events occurring is the sum of their individual probabilities minus the probability of both events occurring: P(A or B) = P(A) + P(B) - P(A and B).
  We are given that P(A) = 0.6 and P(A or B) = 0.96.

Solution:
  We can use the formula for P(A or B) to find P(B):
  P(A or B) = P(A) + P(B) - P(A and B)
  0.96 = 0.6 + P(B) - (0.6 * P(B))  // substituting the given values
  0.96 = 0.6 + 0.4P(B)
  0.36 = 0.4P(B)
  P(B) = 0.36 / 0.4
  P(B) = 0.9

Question: The price of a product is reduced by 30% . By what percentage should it be increased to make it 100%
Choices:
  A: 41.86%
  B: 42.86%
  C: 43.86%
  D: 44.86%
  E: 45.86%
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  If a price is reduced by x%, then the new price is (100-x)% of the original price.
  If a price is increased by y%, then the new price is (100+y)% of the original price.
  
Solution:
  Let the original price be 100.
  After a 30% reduction, the new price is 70.
  To increase the price to 100, we need to increase it by (100-70)/70 = 30/70 = 3/7 = 0.4286 = 42.86%.
  
Action: Answer("B")

  We want to increase the new price to 100%, which means we need to increase it by (100-y)% of the new price.
  So, the final price should be (100-y)% * y% of the original price.
  We can set up an equation to solve for y:
  (100-y)% * y% = 100%
  100y - y^2 = 10000
  y^2 - 100y + 10000 = 0
  (y-50)^2 = 0
  y = 50

  Therefore, the new price is 50% of the original price.
  To increase it to 100%, we need to increase it by (100-50)% = 50% of the new price.
  So, the percentage increase is (50/50) * 100% = 100%.

Topic: Math
Question: Two balls A and B rotate along a circular track. Ball A makes 2 full rotations in 26 minutes. Ball B makes 5 full rotation in 35 minutes. If they start rotating now from the same point, when will they be at the same starting point again?
Choices:
  A: 1 hour and 31 minutes
  B: 2 hour and 31 minutes
  C: 3 hour and 31 minutes
  D: 4 hour and 31 minutes
  E: 5 hour and 31 minutes
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  The time it takes for a ball to make one full rotation is the period of rotation.
  The period of rotation of ball A is 13 minutes (26 minutes for 2 full rotations).
  The period of rotation of ball B is 7 minutes (35 minutes for 5 full rotations).
  The time it takes for two balls to meet again at the starting point is the least common multiple of their periods of rotation.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  The time it takes for a ball to make one full rotation is the period of rotation.
  The period of rotation is the inverse of the frequency of rotation.
  The frequency of rotation is the number of full rotations per unit time.
  If two balls rotate along a circular track with different frequencies, they will meet again at the starting point after a certain amount of time, which is the least common multiple of their periods of rotation.
  We can find the least common multiple by finding the prime factorization of each period of rotation and multiplying the highest power of each prime factor together.
  
Solution:
  The period of rotation of ball A is 26/2 = 13 minutes.
  The frequency of rotation of ball A is 1/13 rotations per minute.
  The period of rotation of ball B is 35/5 = 7 minutes.
  The frequency of rotation of ball B is 1/7 rotations per minute.
  The least common multiple of 13 and 7 is 91, which means that they will meet again at the starting point after 91 minutes.
  Therefore, the answer is 1 hour and 31 minutes.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 1.0 | Problem 18 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A flagstaff 17.5 metre high casts a shadow of length 40.25 metre. The height of building, which casts a shadow of length 28.75 metre under similar conditions will be :
Choices:
  A: 12 metre
  B: 12.5 metre
  C: 13.5 metre
  D: 14 metre
  E: 15 metre
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  If two objects are similar, then the ratio of their corresponding sides is the same.
  In this case, the ratio of the height of the flagstaff to the length of its shadow is the same as the ratio of the height of the building to the length of its shadow.
  Let x be the height of the building.
  We can set up the proportion: 17.5/40.25 = x/28.75 and solve for x.

Action: Answer("B")  
Solving for x: 
  17.5/40.25 = x/28.75
  x = 28.75 * 17.5 / 40.25
  x = 12.5
Therefore, the height of the building is 12.5 meters. Answer: B

  The ratio of the height of an object to the length of its shadow is equal to the ratio of the height of another object to the length of its shadow if both objects are under similar conditions.

Then, we can set up the following proportion:
  17.5 / 40.25 = x / 28.75
Solving for x:
  x = 17.5 * 28.75 / 40.25 = 12.5

  17.5 / 40.25 = x / 28.75
  
Solving for x, we get:
  x = 17.5 * 28.75 / 40.25 = 12.5
  
Action: Answer("B")
Response 5:
Knowledge:
  If two objects are similar, then the ratio of their corresponding sides is the same.
  If a flagstaff of height h casts a shadow of length s, then the height of a building that casts a shadow of length t under similar conditions is given by h*t/s.
  
Action: 
  We can use the above formula to find the height of the building:
  height of building = height of flagstaff * length of shadow of building / length of shadow of flagstaff
  height of building = 17.5 * 28.75 / 40.25
  height of building = 12.5
  Therefore, the height of the building is 12.5 meters.
  Answer: Answer("B")

  We can use this proportion to solve the problem.

Solving for x, we get:

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 1.0 | Problem 20 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: An exam is given in a certain class. The average (arithmetic mean) of the highest score and the lowest score is equal to x. If the average score for the entire class is equal to y and there are z students in the class, where z > 5, then in terms of x, y, and z, what is the average score for the class excluding the highest and lowest scorers?
Choices:
  A: (zy – 2x)/z
  B: (zy – 2)/z
  C: (zx – y)/(z – 2)
  D: (zy – 2x)/(z -2)
  E: (zy – x)/(z + 2)
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Let H be the highest score and L be the lowest score.
  The average of H and L is (H+L)/2.
  The average score for the entire class is the sum of all scores divided by the number of students.
  The sum of all scores is H + L + sum of all other scores.
  The number of students is z.
  We need to find the average score for the class excluding the highest and lowest scorers.
  Let A be the sum of all other scores.
  The number of students who got scores other than H and L is z-2.
  The average score for the class excluding the highest and lowest scorers is A/(z-2).
Action: Answer("D")  
Explanation: 
  We know that (H+L)/2 = x, so H+L = 2x.
  We also know that the average score for the entire class is (H+L+A)/z = y.
  Therefore, H+L+A = yz.
  We want to find A/(z-2).
  We can solve for A by subtracting H and L from both sides of the equation:
  A = yz - (H+L) = yz - 2x.
  Therefore, the average score for the class excluding the highest and lowest scorers is:
  A/(z-2) = (yz - 2x)/(z-2).
  So the answer is D.
Response 1:

  The number of students is z.

  Let S be the sum of all other scores.
  The number of students who took the exam excluding the highest and lowest scorers is z-2.
  The average score for the class excluding the highest and lowest scorers is S/(z-2).
Action: Answer("D")

  We also know that S/z = y, which implies S = yz.
  We want to find the average score for the class excluding the highest and lowest scorers, which is (S - H - L)/(z - 2).
  We can substitute H + L = 2x into the expression for the average score to get (S - H - L)/(z - 2) = (yz - 2x)/(z - 2).

Question: Silu and Meenu were walking on the road.
Silu said, "I weigh 51 Kgs. How much do you weigh?"
Meenu replied that she wouldn't reveal her weight directly as she is overweight.
But she said, "I weigh 29 Kgs plus half of my weight. "How much does Meenu weigh?
Choices:
  A: 12
  B: 28
  C: 27
  D: 58
  E: 91
Response 0:

According to the question, Meenu said, "I weigh 29 Kgs plus half of my weight."

Solving the above equation, we get x = 58 kgs.

x = 58
Therefore, Meenu weighs 58 kgs.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 1.0 | Problem 22 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: An astronaut weighing 211 pounds on Earth would weigh 182 pounds on Venus. The weight of the astronaut on Venus would be approximately what percent of the astronaut’s weight on Earth?
Choices:
  A: 50%
  B: 60%
  C: 70%
  D: 86%
  E: 90%
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Weight on Venus = 182 pounds
  Weight on Earth = 211 pounds
  We need to find the percentage of weight on Venus compared to Earth.
  Percentage = (Weight on Venus / Weight on Earth) * 100
  
Calculation:
  Percentage = (182 / 211) * 100 = 86.26
  
Rounding off to the nearest whole number, the answer is approximately 86%.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  The weight of an object on a planet is proportional to the planet's gravitational force.
  The gravitational force of Venus is about 90% of the gravitational force of Earth.
  To find the percentage decrease in weight, we can use the formula: (weight on Earth - weight on Venus) / weight on Earth * 100%

Action: 
Using the formula above, we get:
  (211 - 182) / 211 * 100% = 13.7%
  
Rounding to the nearest whole number, the weight of the astronaut on Venus is approximately 14% less than the weight of the astronaut on Earth.
To find the weight of the astronaut on Venus as a percentage of the weight on Earth, we can subtract the percentage decrease from 100%:
  100% - 13.7% = 86.3%
  
Therefore, the weight of the astronaut on Venus is approximately 86% of the weight of the astronaut on Earth.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 1.0 | Problem 23 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: At its maximum speed, a space shuttle can travel 700m high in 40 seconds. It will also take 5 seconds to pass a point. What then is the length of the space shuttle?
Choices:
  A: 50 m
  B: 75 m
  C: 100 m
  D: 125 m
  E: 150 m
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  We can use the formula: distance = speed x time
  The shuttle travels 700m in 40 seconds, so its speed is 700/40 = 17.5 m/s
  The shuttle takes 5 seconds to pass a point, so it travels an additional distance of 17.5 x 5 = 87.5 m
  Therefore, the total distance traveled by the shuttle is 700 + 87.5 = 787.5 m
Action: Answer("E")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  We can use the formula: distance = speed x time
  The shuttle travels 700m in 40 seconds, so its speed is 700/40 = 17.5 m/s
  It takes 5 seconds to pass a point, so the distance it covers during that time is 5 x 17.5 = 87.5 m
  The length of the shuttle is the distance it covers during the 5 seconds minus the initial distance it covers in the first second.
  We can calculate the initial distance using the formula: initial distance = (1/2) x acceleration x time^2
  The acceleration due to gravity is 9.8 m/s^2
  So, initial distance = (1/2) x 9.8 x 1^2 = 4.9 m
  
Calculation:
  Length of shuttle = 87.5 m - 4.9 m = 82.6 m

Action: Answer("None of the Above") 

Note: None of the choices match the calculated length of the shuttle, which is approximately 82.6 m.
Response 2:

  Distance = Speed x Time
  The shuttle travels 700m in 40 seconds at maximum speed.
  It takes 5 seconds to pass a point.
  We can use the formula: Distance = Speed x Time to solve for the length of the shuttle.
  We need to find the total distance traveled by the shuttle during the 40 seconds it took to reach a height of 700m plus the distance it traveled during the 5 seconds it took to pass a point.
Action: 
  Total distance traveled = Distance traveled to reach 700m + Distance traveled during 5 seconds
  Distance traveled to reach 700m = 700m
  Speed = Distance / Time = 700m / 40s = 17.5 m/s
  Distance traveled during 5 seconds = Speed x Time = 17.5 m/s x 5s = 87.5m
  Total distance traveled = 700m + 87.5m = 787.5m
  Length of the shuttle = Total distance traveled = 787.5m
  Answer("None of the above")

  The shuttle takes 5 seconds to pass a point, so it travels an additional distance of 17.5 x 5 = 87.5 m
  Therefore, the total distance traveled by the shuttle is 700 + 87.5 = 787.5 m

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 1.0 | Problem 24 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Alice wants to put up fencing around three sides of her rectangular yard and leave one side of 10 meters unfenced. If the yard has an area of 240 square meters, how many meters of fencing does she need?
Choices:
  A: 58
  B: 62
  C: 66
  D: 70
  E: 74
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The area of a rectangle is given by the formula A = l * w, where l is the length and w is the width.
  Alice wants to put up fencing around three sides of her rectangular yard and leave one side of 10 meters unfenced.
  If the yard has an area of 240 square meters, then we have the equation A = l * w = 240.
  We also know that the perimeter of a rectangle is given by the formula P = 2l + 2w.
  Alice wants to fence three sides of the rectangle, so we need to find the perimeter of the rectangle minus the 10 meters that will be left unfenced.

Solution:
  We know that A = l * w = 240.
  We can solve for one of the variables, say w, in terms of the other variable, l, by dividing both sides by l: w = 240 / l.
  We also know that P = 2l + 2w.
  Substituting w = 240 / l, we get P = 2l + 2(240 / l).
  We want to find P - 10, which is the perimeter of the rectangle minus the 10 meters that will be left unfenced.
  So, P - 10 = 2l + 2(240 / l) - 10.
  To minimize the amount of fencing needed, we want to minimize the value of P - 10.
  We can do this by finding the value of l that minimizes the expression 2l + 2(240 / l) - 10.
  Taking the derivative of this expression with respect to l and setting it equal to zero, we get:
  2 - (480 / l^2) = 0
  Solving for l, we get l = sqrt(240) = 4 * sqrt(15).
  Substituting this value of l into the expression for P - 10, we get:
  P - 10 = 2(4 * sqrt(15)) + 2(240 / (4 * sqrt(15))) - 10 = 58.
  Therefore, Alice needs 58 meters of fencing.
Action: Answer("A")

  - x^2 + 20x - 240 = 0
  - (x + 30)(x - 10) = 0
  - x = 10 (since x cannot be negative)
  - The length of the yard is x + 20 = 30 meters, and the width is 8 meters.
  - The total length of fencing needed is 2(30) + 8 + 10 = 78 meters.

Knowledge:
  - The area of a rectangle is given by the formula A = l * w, where A is the area, l is the length, and w is the width.
  - Alice wants to put up fencing around three sides of her rectangular yard and leave one side of 10 meters unfenced. This means that the perimeter of the rectangular yard is P = 2l + w + 10.
  - We can use the area and perimeter to form a system of equations to solve for l and w.

Solution:
  Let l be the length and w be the width of the rectangular yard.
  From the problem, we have:
  A = lw = 240
  P = 2l + w + 10
  We can solve for w in terms of l from the perimeter equation:
  w = P - 2l - 10
  Substituting this into the area equation, we get:
  lw = 240
  l(P - 2l - 10) = 240
  Plugging in the value of P, we get:
  l(2l + w) = 240
  l(2l + P - 2l - 10) = 240
  l(P - 10) = 240
  l = 240 / (P - 10)
  Now we can substitute this value of l into the perimeter equation to solve for P:
  P = 2l + w + 10
  P = 2(240 / (P - 10)) + w + 10
  P(P - 10) = 480 + w(P - 10) + 10P - 100
  P^2 - 10P = 490 + wP
  wP = P^2 - 10P - 490
  w = (P^2 - 10P - 490) / P
  Finally, we can substitute the value of P into the perimeter equation to get the total length of fencing needed:
  Total length of fencing = 2l + 2w + 10
  Total length of fencing = 2(240 / (P - 10)) + 2((P^2 - 10P - 490) / P) + 10

Knowledge:
  The area of a rectangle is given by the formula A = l * w, where l is the length and w is the width.
  Alice wants to put up fencing around three sides of her rectangular yard and leave one side of 10 meters unfenced. This means that the perimeter of the rectangular yard is P = 2l + w + 10.
  We can use the area and perimeter formulas to set up a system of equations to solve for l and w.

Solution:
  Let's start by using the area formula to solve for one of the variables. We can solve for w:
  A = l * w
  240 = l * w
  w = 240 / l

  Now we can substitute this expression for w into the perimeter formula:
  P = 2l + w + 10
  P = 2l + (240 / l) + 10

  We know that Alice wants to fence three sides of the yard, so the total length of fencing she needs is the perimeter of the yard minus the 10 meters of unfenced side:
  F = P - 10
  F = 2l + (240 / l) + 10 - 10
  F = 2l + (240 / l)

  To minimize the amount of fencing needed, we want to find the value of l that minimizes F. We can do this by finding the derivative of F with respect to l and setting it equal to zero:
  dF/dl = 2 - 240 / l^2
  0 = 2 - 240 / l^2
  l^2 = 120
  l = sqrt(120) = 2 * sqrt(30)

  Now we can substitute this value of l into the expression for F to find the minimum amount of fencing needed:
  F = 2l + (240 / l)
  F = 2 * 2 * sqrt(30) + (240 / (2 * sqrt(30)))
  F = 4 * sqrt(30) + 40 / sqrt(30)
  F = (4 * sqrt(30) + 40 / sqrt(30)) * (sqrt(30) / sqrt(30))
  F = (4 * 30 + 40) / sqrt(30)
  F = 70 / sqrt(30)

  We can simplify this expression by multiplying the numerator and denominator by sqrt(30):
  F = 70 / sqrt(30) * sqrt(30) / sqrt(30)
  F = 70 * sqrt(30) / 30
  F = 7 * sqrt(30)

  Therefore, Alice needs approximately 7 * sqrt(30) meters of fencing.

w = (-10 + sqrt(100 + 8P)) / 4

Now we can substitute the value of w into the area formula to solve for l.
l = 240 / w

Finally, we can use the perimeter formula to solve for the amount of fencing needed.
P = 2l + 2w + 10

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 1.0 | Problem 25 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A sporting goods store carries only yellow and white golf balls. At the beginning of the day it had 600 golf balls in stock, and by the end of the day it had sold 80% of its inventory of golf balls. If the store sold an equal number of yellow and white golf balls, and in doing so sold all of its white golf balls, how many yellow golf balls did the store have to begin the day?
Choices:
  A: 80
  B: 120
  C: 240
  D: 320
  E: 360
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  - The store sold 80% of its inventory of golf balls.
  - The store sold an equal number of yellow and white golf balls.
  - The store sold all of its white golf balls.
  - The store had 600 golf balls in stock at the beginning of the day.
  
Let's assume that the store had y yellow golf balls and w white golf balls at the beginning of the day. Since the store sold all of its white golf balls, we know that the number of white golf balls sold is w. We also know that the store sold an equal number of yellow and white golf balls, so the number of yellow golf balls sold is also w. 

We can set up an equation to represent the information given: 

w + w = 0.8(600) 

Simplifying the equation: 

2w = 480 

w = 240 

So the store had 240 white golf balls at the beginning of the day. Since the store had an equal number of yellow and white golf balls, it also had 240 yellow golf balls at the beginning of the day. 

Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  - The store sold 80% of its inventory of golf balls.
  - The store sold an equal number of yellow and white golf balls.
  - The store sold all of its white golf balls.
  - The store had 600 golf balls in stock at the beginning of the day.
  
Let's assume that the store had y yellow golf balls and w white golf balls at the beginning of the day. We know that y + w = 600. We also know that the store sold 80% of its inventory, so it sold 480 golf balls (0.8 * 600). Since the store sold an equal number of yellow and white golf balls, it sold 240 yellow golf balls and 240 white golf balls. We also know that the store sold all of its white golf balls, so w = 0. Therefore, y = 600 - w = 600 - 0 = 600.

  - The store sold an equal number of yellow and white golf balls.
  - The store sold all of its white golf balls.
  - The store had 600 golf balls in stock at the beginning of the day.
  
Let's assume that the store had y yellow golf balls and w white golf balls at the beginning of the day. Since the store sold all of its white golf balls, we know that the number of white golf balls sold is w. We also know that the store sold 80% of its inventory of golf balls, so the total number of golf balls sold is 0.8 * 600 = 480. Since the store sold an equal number of yellow and white golf balls, we know that the number of yellow golf balls sold is also w. Therefore, we can write the following equation:

w + w = 480

Simplifying this equation, we get:

2w = 480

w = 240

So the store had 240 white golf balls at the beginning of the day. Since the store had a total of 600 golf balls in stock at the beginning of the day, we can write another equation:

y + 240 = 600

Solving for y, we get:

y = 360

Therefore, the store had 360 yellow golf balls at the beginning of the day.

Action: Answer("E")

Question: The bus fare for two persons for travelling between Agra and Aligarh id four-thirds the train fare between the same places for one person. The total fare paid by 6 persons travelling by bus and 8 persons travelling by train between the two places is Rs.1512. Find the train fare between the two places for one person?
Choices:
  A: 126
  B: 77
  C: 88
  D: 66
  E: 54
Response 0:

The total fare paid by 6 persons travelling by bus will be (6/2) * (4/3)x = 8x.
The total fare paid by 8 persons travelling by train will be 8x.
The sum of the total fares is given as Rs. 1512.
Therefore, 8x + 8x = 1512
Simplifying the equation, we get:
16x = 1512
x = 94.5
Therefore, the train fare between the two places for one person is Rs. 94.5.

Topic: Math
Question: Jim filled his dog's bowl with dog food. Starting at 8:00 am, Jim's dog ate exactly once an hour, consuming exactly 1/3 of the dog food remaining in the bowl at each feeding session. Approximately, what percent of the original food was in the dog's bowl right before the dog began to eat at noon of the same day?
Choices:
  A: 20%
  B: 25%
  C: 30%
  D: 35%
  E: 40%
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  If the dog eats 1/3 of the remaining food at each feeding session, then the amount of food remaining after each feeding session is 2/3 of the previous amount.
  The dog ate 4 times (from 8:00 am to 11:00 am) and consumed 1/3 of the remaining food at each feeding session.
  Therefore, the amount of food remaining in the bowl at noon is (2/3)^4 of the original amount.
Action: Answer("C")  
Explanation: 
  The amount of food remaining in the bowl at noon is (2/3)^4 of the original amount, which is approximately 30.86% of the original amount. 
  Therefore, the answer is approximately 30%, which is choice C.
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  From 8:00 am to 12:00 pm, the dog ate 4 times.
  At each feeding session, the dog ate 1/3 of the remaining food.
  Therefore, the amount of food remaining after each feeding session can be represented by the sequence: 1, 2/3, 4/9, 8/27.
  To find the percent of the original food remaining, we need to multiply the final fraction by 100%.
Action: Answer("D")  
To calculate the final fraction, we can multiply the fractions in the sequence: 1 * 2/3 * 4/9 * 8/27 = 64/729.
To convert this fraction to a percentage, we can divide the numerator by the denominator, then multiply by 100%: (64/729) * 100% = 8.77% (rounded to two decimal places).
Therefore, approximately 35% of the original food was in the dog's bowl right before the dog began to eat at noon.

  The dog did not eat anything between 11:00 am and noon.
  
Solution:

  At 9:00 am, the dog ate 1/3 of the remaining 100 units, leaving 2/3 * 100 = 66.67 units.
  At 10:00 am, the dog ate 1/3 of the remaining 66.67 units, leaving 2/3 * 66.67 = 44.44 units.
  At 11:00 am, the dog ate 1/3 of the remaining 44.44 units, leaving 2/3 * 44.44 = 29.63 units.
  At noon, the dog did not eat anything, so there were still 29.63 units of food in the bowl.
  Therefore, the percent of the original food remaining in the bowl at noon is 29.63%.

Question: Anna is able to buy 5 more articles for $300 after the price of each article decreased by 15%. What is the new selling price of each article?
Choices:
  A: $8
  B: $10
  C: $13.6
  D: $22.9
  E: $40
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  If the price of each article decreased by 15%, then the new price is 85% of the original price.
  Anna was able to buy 5 more articles for $300, which means that the price of each article decreased by $60 ($300/5).
  Therefore, the original price of each article was $400 ($300 + $60) and the new price is $340 ($400 x 85%).
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  If the price of each article decreased by 15%, then the new price is 85% of the original price.
  Anna was able to buy 5 more articles for $300, which means that each article costs $60 ($300/5).
  If Anna was able to buy 5 more articles, then she was originally planning to buy 15 articles (10 + 5).
  Let x be the original price of each article.
  The total cost of 15 articles at the original price is 15x.
  The total cost of 15 articles at the new price is 15(0.85x) = 12.75x.
  We know that 15x = 300 + 5x, which simplifies to 10x = 300, so x = 30.
  Therefore, the new selling price of each article is 0.85x = 0.85(30) = $25.5.
Action: Answer("None of the Above")  
Note: None of the above choices is the correct answer. The correct answer is $25.5.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 1.0 | Problem 29 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A rope 20 meters long is cut into two pieces. If the length of one piece of rope is 3 meters shorter than the length of the other, what is the length, in meters, of the longer piece of rope?
Choices:
  A: 7.5
  B: 8.9
  C: 9.9
  D: 11.5
  E: 11.7
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  Let x be the length of the longer piece of rope.
  Then, the length of the shorter piece of rope is x - 3.
  The sum of the lengths of the two pieces of rope is 20 meters.
  Therefore, x + (x - 3) = 20.
  Simplifying the equation, we get 2x - 3 = 20.
  Solving for x, we get x = 11.5.
  Therefore, the length of the longer piece of rope is 11.5 meters.

  Therefore, the length of the longer piece of rope is 11.5 meters.

Topic: Math
Question: In a survey of students, each student selected from a list of 10 songs the 2 songs that the student liked best. If each song was selected 5 times, how many students were surveyed?
Choices:
  A: 96
  B: 48
  C: 32
  D: 25
  E: 18
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  If each song was selected 5 times, and each student selected 2 songs, then there were 5/2 = 2.5 students who selected each song.
  To find the total number of students surveyed, we can divide the total number of song selections by the average number of songs selected per student.
  The total number of song selections is 10 songs * 5 selections per song = 50 selections.
  The average number of songs selected per student is 2, since each student selected 2 songs.
  Therefore, the total number of students surveyed is 50 selections / 2 songs per student = 25 students.
Action: Answer("D")

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 1.0 | Problem 31 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: The original retail price of an appliance was 60 percent more than its wholesale cost. If the appliance was actually sold for 20 percent less than the original retail price, then it was sold for what percent more than its wholesale cost?
Choices:
  A: 20%
  B: 28%
  C: 36%
  D: 40%
  E: 42%
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Let's assume the wholesale cost of the appliance is "x".
  The original retail price of the appliance is 60% more than its wholesale cost, which means the original retail price is (100% + 60%) = 160% of the wholesale cost. So, the original retail price is 1.6x.
  The appliance was sold for 20% less than the original retail price, which means it was sold for (100% - 20%) = 80% of the original retail price. So, the selling price is 0.8(1.6x) = 1.28x.
  We need to find the percentage more than the wholesale cost that the appliance was sold for. 
  The percentage increase is ((selling price - wholesale cost) / wholesale cost) * 100.
Action: Answer("B")  
  Plugging in the values, we get ((1.28x - x) / x) * 100 = 28%. Therefore, the appliance was sold for 28% more than its wholesale cost. So, the answer is (B) 28%.
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Let W be the wholesale cost of the appliance.
  The original retail price of the appliance was 60% more than its wholesale cost, so it was sold for 1.6W.
  The appliance was actually sold for 20% less than the original retail price, so it was sold for 0.8(1.6W) = 1.28W.
  The percent increase from the wholesale cost to the actual selling price is (1.28W - W)/W * 100% = 28%.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 2:
Knowledge:
  Let W be the wholesale cost of the appliance.

  The difference between the selling price and the wholesale cost is 1.28W - W = 0.28W.
  The percent increase over the wholesale cost is (0.28W/W) x 100% = 28%.
Action: Answer("B")

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 1.0 | Problem 32 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: When folded into two equal halves a rectangular sheet had a perimeter of 48cm for each part folded along one set of sides and the same is 66cm when folded along the other set of sides. Find the area of the sheet.
Choices:
  A: 1584
  B: 1120
  C: 792
  D: 1320
  E: 1200
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  When a rectangular sheet is folded into two equal halves along one set of sides, the perimeter of each part is half of the original perimeter.
  The perimeter of a rectangle is given by the formula P = 2(l + w), where l and w are the length and width of the rectangle, respectively.
  The area of a rectangle is given by the formula A = lw.
  
Action: 
  Let the length and width of the rectangular sheet be l and w, respectively.
  When folded along the length, each part has a perimeter of 48/2 = 24 cm, so we have:
  2(l/2 + w) = 24
  l + 2w = 24
  
  When folded along the width, each part has a perimeter of 66/2 = 33 cm, so we have:
  2(l + w/2) = 33
  2l + w = 33
  
  Solving the system of equations, we get l = 15 and w = 6.
  Therefore, the area of the rectangular sheet is A = lw = 15 x 6 = 90 cm^2.
  Answer: Answer("None of the Above") - The correct answer is not among the choices.
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  When a rectangular sheet is folded into two equal halves along one set of sides, the perimeter of each part is half of the original perimeter.
  The perimeter of a rectangle is given by the formula: P = 2(l + w), where l is the length and w is the width.
  The area of a rectangle is given by the formula: A = lw.
  
Action: 
  Let the length and width of the rectangular sheet be l and w, respectively.
  When folded along the length, each part has a perimeter of 66/2 = 33cm.
  Therefore, 2(l + w/2) = 33, which simplifies to l + w/2 = 16.5.
  When folded along the width, each part has a perimeter of 48/2 = 24cm.
  Therefore, 2(w + l/2) = 24, which simplifies to w + l/2 = 12.
  Solving the above two equations simultaneously, we get l = 11 and w = 6.
  Therefore, the area of the rectangular sheet is lw = 11 x 6 = 66 sq.cm.
  Answer: Answer("E")

Response 3:
Knowledge:
  When a rectangular sheet is folded into two equal halves, the perimeter of each part is half of the original perimeter.
  Let's say the length and width of the rectangular sheet are l and w, respectively.
  When folded along the length, the perimeter of each part is 66cm, so we have 2(l/2 + w) = 66, which simplifies to l + 2w = 66.
  When folded along the width, the perimeter of each part is 48cm, so we have 2(l + w/2) = 48, which simplifies to 2l + w = 48.
  We need to find the area of the sheet, which is lw.

Solution:
  From the two equations we have, we can solve for l and w:
  l = 66 - 2w
  2l + w = 48
  Substitute the first equation into the second equation:
  2(66 - 2w) + w = 48
  132 - 3w = 48
  3w = 84
  w = 28
  l = 66 - 2w = 10
  The area of the sheet is lw = 280.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 1.0 | Problem 33 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: On a normal day Bill usually averages about 15 mph when riding his bicycle. On a windy day, his speed is reduced by 4 mph. How far can Bill travel on a windy day in 21 minutes? Round to the nearest hundredth.
Choices:
  A: 2 miles
  B: 2.25 miles
  C: 3.25 miles
  D: 3.85 miles
  E: 2.85 miles
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  - Distance = Speed x Time
  - Bill's normal speed = 15 mph
  - On a windy day, his speed is reduced by 4 mph, so his speed is 15 - 4 = 11 mph
  - Time = 21 minutes = 0.35 hours
Calculation:
  - Distance = Speed x Time = 11 mph x 0.35 hours = 3.85 miles
Action: Answer("D")

Choices:
  A: 90
  B: 80
  C: 95

Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The ratio of red sweets to green sweets is 3:4.
  This means that for every 3 red sweets, there are 4 green sweets.
  We are given that there are 120 green sweets in the bag.
  
Calculation:
  If the ratio of red sweets to green sweets is 3:4, then the total ratio is 3+4=7.
  This means that for every 7 sweets, 3 are red and 4 are green.
  To find out how many red sweets there are, we need to set up a proportion:
  4/7 = 120/x
  where x is the number of red sweets.
  Solving for x, we get:
  x = 120*3/4 = 90
  
Action: Answer("A")

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 1.0 | Problem 35 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A number of friends decided to go on a picnic and planned to spend Rs. 96 on eatables. Four of them, however, did not turn up. As a consequence, the remaining ones had to contribute Rs. 4 extra, each. The number of those who attended the picnic was
Choices:
  A: 8
  B: 12
  C: 16
  D: 24
  E: 25
Response 0:
Let's assume that the total number of friends who planned to go on the picnic was "x". Therefore, the cost per person would be 96/x. 

When 4 friends did not turn up, the remaining friends had to contribute Rs. 4 extra each. So, the new cost per person became (96/x) + 4.

We can set up an equation based on the above information:
96/x = (96/x + 4) * (x-4)/x

Simplifying the equation, we get:
96 = (96 + 4x - 384)/x

Multiplying both sides by x, we get:
96x = 4x^2 - 288x + 384*4

Simplifying further, we get:
4x^2 - 384x + 1536 = 0

Dividing both sides by 4, we get:
x^2 - 96x + 384 = 0

Using the quadratic formula, we get:
x = (96 ± sqrt(96^2 - 4*384))/2
x = (96 ± sqrt(9216 - 1536))/2
x = (96 ± sqrt(7680))/2
x = (96 ± 8*sqrt(30))/2

x = 48 ± 4*sqrt(30)

Since the number of friends cannot be a decimal, we can round off to the nearest integer:
x = 48 + 4*sqrt(30) ≈ 68.6, rounded to 69

Therefore, the number of friends who attended the picnic was:
x - 4 = 69 - 4 = 65

Action: Answer("None of the Above") 

Note: None of the given choices match the calculated answer of 65.
Response 1:
Let's assume that the total number of friends who planned to go on the picnic was "x". 
The total amount they planned to spend was Rs. 96. 
So, the amount each friend would have to contribute would be 96/x. 

But, 4 friends did not turn up, so the remaining friends had to contribute Rs. 4 extra each. 
So, the new amount each friend contributed was (96/x) + 4. 

The total amount collected after 4 friends did not turn up would be (96/x + 4) * (x-4). 
This is because the remaining friends had to contribute Rs. 4 extra each. 

We know that the total amount collected after 4 friends did not turn up was still Rs. 96. 
So, we can equate the two expressions: 

(96/x + 4) * (x-4) = 96 

Simplifying this expression, we get: 

96 + 4x - 384/x - 16 = 96 

4x - 384/x = 16 

4(x^2 - 96) / x = 16 

x^2 - 96 = 4x 

x^2 - 4x - 96 = 0 

Solving this quadratic equation, we get: 

x = 12 or x = -8 

Since we cannot have negative number of friends, the answer is:

Topic: Math
Question: there are more than 501 students in a school such that 20% of them exactly took physics and 28% of them exactly took math. What could be the least possible no of students in the school?
Choices:
  A: 550
  B: 570
  C: 600
  D: 700
  E: none of these
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  - We know that there are more than 501 students in the school.
  - We know that 20% of the students took physics and 28% of the students took math.
  - We don't know if there is any overlap between the students who took physics and the students who took math.
  - To find the minimum number of students, we need to assume that all the students who took physics are also included in the students who took math.
  - To find the minimum number of students, we need to assume that there are no other students in the school who did not take physics or math.

Calculation:
  - Let's assume that all the students who took physics are also included in the students who took math.
  - Then, the percentage of students who took math or physics is 20% + (28% - 20%) = 28.4%.
  - Let's set up an inequality to find the minimum number of students: 28.4% of the number of students > 501.
  - Solving for the number of students: number of students > 501 / 0.284 = 1764.08.
  - The minimum number of students is the smallest integer greater than 1764.08, which is 1765.

Action: Answer("E") none of these.
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  - We know that there are more than 501 students in the school.
  - 20% of the students took physics and 28% of the students took math.
  - We want to find the least possible number of students in the school.
  - We can use the fact that the total number of students is at least the number of students who took physics divided by 20% (or 0.2), and similarly for math.

Calculation:
  - Let's assume that the number of students in the school is x.
  - Then, the number of students who took physics is 0.2x.
  - The number of students who took math is 0.28x.
  - The total number of students is at least 0.2x/0.2 + 0.28x/0.28 = x + x = 2x.
  - We know that 2x > 501, so x > 250.5.
  - The least possible integer value of x that satisfies this inequality is 251.
  - Therefore, the least possible number of students in the school is 251.

Question: Two cars are travelling from the same starting point in the same direction, having started their commute at the same time. The first car travels at a steady rate of 55 mph, while the second travels at a steady rate of 52 mph. How much time will pass before the cars are 15 miles away from each other?
Choices:
  A: 3 hours
  B: 5 hours
  C: 6 hours
  D: 4 hours
  E: 7 hours
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The relative speed between the two cars is the difference between their speeds, which is 55 - 52 = 3 mph.
  We want to know how much time it will take for the distance between the two cars to be 15 miles.
  We can use the formula: time = distance / speed
  
Action: 
  Let's use the formula to find the answer:
  The time it takes for the cars to be 15 miles apart is: time = distance / speed = 15 / 3 = 5 hours.
  Answer: B

  The number of ways to choose breakfast and dinner is the product of the number of ways to choose each meal.

  [2x] denotes the greatest integer less than or equal to (2x).
  [2y] denotes the greatest integer less than or equal to (2y).
  Therefore, [x], [y], [x + y], [2x], and [2y] are all integers.
  Since L(x,y) and R(x,y) are both sums of integers, they are also integers.
  Therefore, we need to find two positive real numbers x and y for which two integers are equal, not equal, one is less than the other, and one is greater than the other.
Action: Answer("E")
Response 9:
Knowledge:
  [x] denotes the greatest integer less than or equal to x.
  L(x,y) = [x] + [y] + [x + y]
  R(x,y) = [2x] + [2y]
  We need to find two positive real numbers x and y for which L(x,y) = R(x,y), L(x,y) ≠ R(x,y), L(x,y) < R(x,y), or L(x,y) > R(x,y).

Analysis:
  Let's consider the case when x = 1.5 and y = 1.5.
  Then, [x] = 1, [y] = 1, [x+y] = 3, [2x] = 3, and [2y] = 3.
  Therefore, L(x,y) = 1 + 1 + 3 = 5 and R(x,y) = 3 + 3 = 6.
  So, L(x,y) < R(x,y).
  This means that option D is not correct.

Topic: Math
Question: While selling a watch, a shopkeeper gives a discount of 5%. If he gives a discount of 7%, he earns Rs. 15 less as profit. The marked price of the watch is:
Choices:
  A: Rs. 697.50
  B: Rs. 712.50
  C: Rs. 787.50
  D: Rs. 750
  E: Rs. 780
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Let's assume the marked price of the watch is M.
  The shopkeeper gives a discount of 5%, so the selling price of the watch is 0.95M.
  The shopkeeper gives a discount of 7%, so the selling price of the watch is 0.93M.
  The difference between the selling prices is Rs. 15.
  So, 0.95M - 0.93M = 15
  0.02M = 15
  M = 750
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Let the marked price of the watch be M.
  Let the cost price of the watch be C.
  Let the profit earned by the shopkeeper be P.
  When the shopkeeper gives a discount of 5%, the selling price of the watch is 0.95M.
  When the shopkeeper gives a discount of 7%, the selling price of the watch is 0.93M.
  We can set up the following equations:
    0.95M - C = P
    0.93M - C = P + 15
  We can solve for M by eliminating P:
    0.95M - C = 0.93M - C - 15
    0.02M = 15
    M = 750
  Therefore, the marked price of the watch is Rs. 750.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 2:
Knowledge:
  Let the marked price of the watch be M.
  Let the cost price of the watch be C.
  Let the profit earned by the shopkeeper be P.
  When the shopkeeper gives a discount of 5%, the selling price of the watch is 0.95M.
  When the shopkeeper gives a discount of 7%, the selling price of the watch is 0.93M.
  We can set up the following equation based on the given information:
    P = M - C
    P = 0.95M - C
    P + 15 = 0.93M - C
  We can solve for C in terms of P and M using the first two equations:
    C = M - P
    C = 0.95M - P
  We can substitute these expressions for C in the third equation and solve for M:
    P + 15 = 0.93M - (M - P)
    P + 15 = 0.93M - M + P
    15 = 0.07M
    M = 15/0.07

Topic: Math
Question: I have a money pouch containing Rs. 700. There are equal number of 25 paise coins, 50 paise coins and one rupee coins.
How many of each are there?
Choices:
  A: 453
  B: 651
  C: 400
  D: 487
  E: 286
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  100 paise = 1 rupee
  Let's assume there are 'x' coins of each denomination.
  Total value of 25 paise coins = 0.25x
  Total value of 50 paise coins = 0.50x
  Total value of 1 rupee coins = 1x = x
  Total value of all coins = 0.25x + 0.50x + x = 1.75x
  We know that the total value of all coins is Rs. 700, so:
  1.75x = 700
  x = 400
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Let's start by setting up an equation to represent the given information. Let x be the number of each type of coin. Then we know that:

0.25x + 0.50x + 1.00x = 700

Simplifying this equation, we get:

1.75x = 700

Dividing both sides by 1.75, we get:

x = 400

Therefore, there are 400 of each type of coin.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 1.0 | Problem 43 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: The height of a room to its semi-perimeter is 2:5. It costs Rs.260 to paper the walls of the room with paper 50cm wide at Rs.2 per meter allowing an area of 15 sq.m for doors and windows. The height of the room is:
Choices:
  A: 2.6m
  B: 3.9m
  C: 4m
  D: 4.2m
  E: 4.4m
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  1. The semi-perimeter of a room is half the sum of the lengths of all its sides.
  2. The cost of papering the walls of a room is equal to the perimeter of the room multiplied by the cost per meter of the paper.
  3. The area of a rectangle is equal to its length multiplied by its width.
  
Let the height of the room be 2x and the semi-perimeter be 5y. Then, the length of the room is 5y - 2x and the width of the room is y. 

The perimeter of the room is 2(5y - 2x) + 2y = 10y - 4x + 2y = 12y - 4x. 

The cost of papering the walls is (12y - 4x)(2/100) = (6y - 2x)(1/50) = (3y - x)(1/25) * 520. 

The area of the doors and windows is 15 sq.m, so the area of the walls is (5y - 2x)(2x) - 15. 

(5y - 2x)(2x) - 15 = 2x(10y - 4x - 15) = 20xy - 8x^2 - 30x. 

(3y - x)(1/25) * 520 = 260. 

3y - x = 5. 

Substituting 3y - x = 5 into 20xy - 8x^2 - 30x = 0, we get 20xy - 8x^2 - 30x = 20(5 + x)x - 8x^2 - 30x = 0. 

Simplifying, we get 8x^2 + 10x - 100 = 0. 

Solving for x using the quadratic formula, we get x = 2.5 or x = -5. 

Since the height of the room cannot be negative, the height of the room is 2x = 5. 

Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  1. The semi-perimeter of a room is half of the sum of the lengths of all its sides.
  2. The cost of papering the walls of a room is equal to the perimeter of the room multiplied by the cost per meter of the paper.
  3. The area of the doors and windows is subtracted from the total area of the walls to get the area of the walls that need to be papered.
  4. The height of the room is related to the semi-perimeter of the room.

Let the height of the room be 2x and the semi-perimeter be 5y. Then, the length of the room is 5y - 4x.
The area of the walls that need to be papered is (5y + 5y - 4x) * 2x = 10xy - 8x^2.
The cost of papering the walls is (10xy - 8x^2) * 2 / 100 * 2 = (40xy - 32x^2) / 100.
The total area of the walls is 2x * (5y + 5y - 4x) = 20xy - 8x^2.
The area of the doors and windows is 15 sq.m = 15000 sq.cm.
So, (5y - 2x) * (5y - 2x) = 15000 + 8x^2.
Solving for y, we get y = (2x + 50) / 5.

Substituting y in terms of x in the expression for the cost of papering the walls, we get:
(40x(2x + 50)/5 - 32x^2) / 100 = 260
Simplifying, we get 4x^2 + 20x - 325 = 0
Solving for x, we get x = 4.25 or x = -7.25. Since the height of the room cannot be negative, we choose x = 4.25.

Therefore, the height of the room is 2x = 2 * 4.25 = 8.5 meters.

  2. Let the height of the room be 2x and the semi-perimeter be 5y. Then, the perimeter of the room is 10y.
  3. Cost of papering the walls = cost of paper required
  4. Area of the four walls = height * semi-perimeter * 2
  5. Area of doors and windows = 15 sq.m
  6. Width of paper = 50 cm = 0.5 m
  7. Cost of paper per meter = Rs.2
  8. Total cost of paper = cost of paper per meter * length of paper required
  
Calculation:
  1. Let the height of the room be 2x and the semi-perimeter be 5y.
  2. Then, the perimeter of the room is 10y.
  3. Height to semi-perimeter ratio = 2:5
  4. So, 2x/5y = 2/5
  5. Cross-multiplying, we get 2y = x
  6. Area of the four walls = height * semi-perimeter * 2 = 2x * 5y * 2 = 20xy
  7. Area of doors and windows = 15 sq.m
  8. Area of the walls to be papered = Area of the four walls - Area of doors and windows = 20xy - 15
  9. Length of paper required = (Area of the walls to be papered) / (width of paper) = (20xy - 15) / 0.5 = 40xy - 30
  10. Cost of paper required = (length of paper required) * (cost of paper per meter) = (40xy - 30) * 2 = 80xy - 60
  11. Cost of papering the walls = Rs.260
  12. So, 80xy - 60 = 260
  13. Simplifying, we get 8xy - 6 = 26
  14. 8xy = 32
  15. xy = 4
  16. Substituting xy = 4 in 2y = x, we get y = 2 and x = 4
  17. So, the height of the room is 2x = 8 meters.

Response 9:
Knowledge:
  1. The semi-perimeter of a room is half of the sum of the lengths of all its sides.
  2. The cost of papering the walls of a room is the product of the perimeter of the room and the cost per unit length of the paper.
  3. The area of a rectangle is the product of its length and width.
  
Let the height of the room be 2x and the semi-perimeter be 5y. Then, the length of the room is 5y - 2x and the width of the room is y. 

The perimeter of the room is 2(5y - 2x) + 2y = 10y - 4x + 2y = 12y - 4x. 

The cost of papering the walls is (12y - 4x)(2/100) = (3y - x)(1/25)Rs. 

The area of the doors and windows is 15 sq.m, so the area of the walls is (5y - 2x)(2x) - 15 = 10xy - 4x^2 - 15. 

We can now set up the following equation: 

(3y - x)/25 = 260/(10xy - 4x^2 - 15)

Simplifying this equation, we get: 

300xy - 100x^2 - 375 = 13y - 3x

We also know that the height of the room to its semi-perimeter is 2:5, so we have: 

2/5 = 2x/5y 

Simplifying this equation, we get: 

x/y = 1/2 

Multiplying both sides by y, we get: 

x = y/2 

Substituting this into the equation we obtained earlier, we get: 

300y^2/2 - 100y^2/4 - 375 = 13y - 3y/2 

Simplifying this equation, we get: 

75y^2 - 104y + 750 = 0 

Solving for y using the quadratic formula, we get: 

y = 2.8 or y = 10/3 

Substituting y = 2.8 into x = y/2, we get: 

x = 1.4 

Therefore, the height of the room is 2x = 2(1.4) = 2.8m. 

Action: Answer("A")
Votes: B, N, A, E, E, E, E, C, E, A

Question: If one third of 3/4 of a number is 21. Then, find the number?
Choices:
  A: 84
  B: 66
  C: 28
  D: 19
  E: 11

  "3/4 of" means 3/4 multiplied by the number.
  We need to solve for the number.
  
Solution:

So, (1/3)*(3/4)*x = 21
Simplifying the equation, we get:
(1/4)*x = 21
Multiplying both sides by 4, we get:
x = 84

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 1.0 | Problem 46 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: The difference between the squares of two numbers is 256000 and the sum of the numbers is 1000. The numbers are
Choices:
  A: 600, 400
  B: 628, 372
  C: 640, 360
  D: None of these
  E: Cannot be determined
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Let x and y be the two numbers.
  The difference between the squares of two numbers is (x^2 - y^2) = (x + y)(x - y).
  The sum of the numbers is x + y = 1000.
  
Calculation:
  (x + y)(x - y) = x^2 - y^2 = 256000
  x + y = 1000
  Let a = x + y = 1000
  Let b = x - y
  Then a*b = 256000
  We need to solve for a and b, and then solve for x and y.
  Factor 256000 = 2^10 * 5^3
  Since a*b = 256000 and a > b, we can try different pairs of factors of 256000 until we find a pair that adds up to 1000.
  Possible pairs of factors are (2^5, 5^3), (2^6, 5^2), (2^8, 5), (2^10, 1)
  The pair (2^8, 5) adds up to 2^8 * 5 + 2^2 * 5^3 = 1280 + 1250 = 2530, which is too large.
  The pair (2^6, 5^2) adds up to 2^6 * 5^2 + 2^4 * 5^2 = 1600, which is too small.
  The pair (2^5, 5^3) adds up to 2^5 * 5^3 + 2^5 * 5^2 = 4000, which is too large.
  The pair (2^10, 1) adds up to 2^10 + 1 = 1025, which is too small.
  Therefore, there is no integer solution for a and b, and hence no integer solution for x and y.

Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Let x and y be the two numbers.
  The difference between the squares of two numbers is (x^2 - y^2) = (x + y)(x - y).
  The sum of the numbers is x + y = 1000.
  
Calculation:
  We know that (x^2 - y^2) = 256000.
  We can factor 256000 as 256000 = 400 * 640.
  We can write (x + y)(x - y) = 400 * 640.
  Since x + y = 1000, we have (x - y) = (400 * 640) / 1000 = 256.
  Adding (x + y) and (x - y), we get 2x = 1000 + 256 = 1256.
  Therefore, x = 628 and y = 372.

Response 3:
Knowledge:
  Let x and y be the two numbers.
  The difference between the squares of two numbers is (x^2 - y^2) = (x + y)(x - y).
  The sum of the numbers is x + y = 1000.
  
Calculation:
  We know that (x^2 - y^2) = 256000.
  We also know that (x + y) = 1000.
  We can use these two equations to solve for x and y.
  (x^2 - y^2) = (x + y)(x - y) = 256000
  (x + y) = 1000
  (x - y) = 256000 / (x + y)
  Adding the last two equations, we get:
  2x = 1000 + 256000 / (x + y)
  Multiplying both sides by (x + y), we get:
  2x(x + y) = 1000(x + y) + 256000
  2x^2 + 2xy = 1000x + 1000y + 256000
  We can substitute (x + y) with 1000 to get:
  2x^2 + 2xy = 1000x + 1000y + 256000
  2x^2 + 2xy = 1000x + 1000(1000 - x) + 256000
  2x^2 + 2xy = 1000x + 1000000 - 1000x + 256000
  2x^2 + 2xy = 2x^2 + 1256000
  xy = 628 * 372 = 233016

Now we need to find the two numbers that satisfy the conditions.
We know that x + y = 1000, and xy = 233016.
We can solve for x and y using the quadratic formula:
x = (1000 ± sqrt(1000^2 - 4*1*(-233016))) / (2*1) = 628 or 372
y = 1000 - x = 372 or 628

Therefore, the two numbers are 628 and 372.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 1.0 | Problem 47 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A company produces 420 units of a particular computer component every month, at a production cost to the company of $110 per component, and sells all of the components by the end of each month. What is the minimum selling price per component that will guarantee that the yearly profit (revenue from sales minus production costs) will be at least $626,400 ?
Choices:
  A: 226
  B: 230
  C: 240
  D: 260
  E: 280
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The company produces 420 units of a computer component every month.
  The production cost of each component is $110.
  The yearly profit should be at least $626,400.
  
Calculation:
  The yearly production cost is 420 * 12 * $110 = $554,400.
  The yearly profit should be at least $626,400, so the yearly revenue should be at least $1,180,800.
  The revenue per component is $1,180,800 / (420 * 12) = $233.33 (rounded to the nearest cent).
  The minimum selling price per component that will guarantee the yearly profit is at least $233.33 + $110 = $343.33.
  The answer that is closest to $343.33 is choice B.
Action: Answer("B")

  The distance between the starting point and the final point is the hypotenuse of a right-angled triangle with sides 3km and 4km.
  Using Pythagoras theorem, the distance between the starting point and the final point is sqrt(3^2 + 4^2) = 5km.

Question: A cyclist travels at 12 miles per hour. How many minutes will it take to travel 48 miles?
Choices:
  A: 1
  B: 240
  C: 30
  D: 60
  E: 120

  - The cyclist travels at 12 miles per hour.
  - The distance to be traveled is 48 miles.
  
Calculation:

  - time = 48 miles / 12 miles per hour
  - time = 4 hours
  - 4 hours = 4 * 60 minutes = 240 minutes

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 1.0 | Problem 54 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Everyone in the family earns money each month. If the total income of a family per month is $9000 and the median income is $3000, how many members are there in the family?
Choices:
  A: 2
  B: 3
  C: 4
  D: 5
  E: 6
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  - Median is the middle value in a sorted list of numbers.
  - If the median income is $3000, then there are an equal number of family members earning less than $3000 and an equal number of family members earning more than $3000.
  - If the total income of the family is $9000, then the average income per family member is $9000 divided by the number of family members.
Action: 
  - Let's assume there are 'n' family members.
  - If the median income is $3000, then there are (n/2) family members earning less than $3000 and (n/2) family members earning more than $3000.
  - Therefore, the total income of family members earning less than $3000 is (n/2) * $3000 = $1500n.
  - Similarly, the total income of family members earning more than $3000 is also $1500n.
  - Since the total income of the family is $9000, we can write the following equation: $1500n + $1500n = $9000
  - Solving for 'n', we get n = 3.
  - Therefore, there are 3 family members.
Answer: Answer("B")

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 1.0 | Problem 55 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A starts a business with Rs.40,000. After 2 months, B joined him with Rs.60,000. C joined them after some more time with Rs.120,000. At the end of the year, out of a total profit of Rs.375,000, C gets Rs.150,000 as his share. How many months after B joined the business, did C join?
Choices:
  A: 2 months
  B: 4 months
  C: 23 months
  D: 24 months
  E: 84 months
Response 0:
Let's first calculate the total amount invested by A and B for the whole year. A invested for 12 months, and B invested for 10 months (since he joined after 2 months). So, the total investment by A and B is (40000*12) + (60000*10) = 12,00,000 + 6,00,000 = 18,00,000.

Now, let's calculate the investment of C. Let's assume C joined after x months. So, his investment will be (120000 * (12-x)).

Total profit is Rs.375,000, and C gets Rs.150,000 as his share. So, the remaining profit (after giving C his share) is Rs.225,000.

Now, we can use the concept of profit sharing ratio to find the ratio in which A and B will share the remaining profit. Since A invested for 12 months and B invested for 10 months, their profit sharing ratio will be (12*40000) : (10*60000) = 480000 : 600000 = 8:10 = 4:5.

So, A's share of the remaining profit is (4/9)*225000 = 100000, and B's share is (5/9)*225000 = 125000.

Therefore, the total profit share of C is 150000, and the total profit share of A and B is 100000+125000 = 225000. This means that C's profit share is more than the total profit share of A and B. This can only happen if C joined after A and B had already made some profit. So, C must have joined after 2+10 = 12 months.

Since C joined after x months, we have x = 12. Therefore, C joined after 12 months.

Topic: Math
Question: The monthly salary S of a shop assistant is the sum of a fixed salary of $500 plus 5% of all monthly sales. What should the monthly sales be so that her monthly salary reaches $1500?
Choices:
  A: $50000
  B: $40000
  C: $30000
  D: $20000
  E: None of these
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The monthly salary S of a shop assistant is the sum of a fixed salary of $500 plus 5% of all monthly sales.
  We need to find the monthly sales that will make the monthly salary reach $1500.
  We can set up an equation to solve for the monthly sales.
  Let x be the monthly sales.
  Then, S = 500 + 0.05x
  We want S to be equal to 1500.
  So, 1500 = 500 + 0.05x
  Solving for x, we get x = (1500 - 500) / 0.05 = 20000

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 1.0 | Problem 57 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: The sum of k consecutive integers is 51. If the least integer is -50, then k =
Choices:
  A: 40
  B: 62
  C: 82
  D: 92
  E: 102
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The sum of k consecutive integers starting from n is given by k(n + (n+k-1))/2.
  We can use this formula to solve the problem.
  
Action: 
  Let's use the formula to solve the problem.
  We know that the sum of k consecutive integers is 51, and the least integer is -50.
  So, we have k(-50 + (-50+k-1))/2 = 51.
  Simplifying this equation, we get k(2k-99) = 204.
  Factoring 204, we get 204 = 2 x 2 x 3 x 17.
  We can check which of the answer choices gives us a factorization of 204 in the form k(2k-99).
  Trying answer choice A, we get k(2k-99) = 40 x (-79), which does not give us a factorization of 204.
  Trying answer choice B, we get k(2k-99) = 31 x 4 x 17, which gives us a factorization of 204.
  Therefore, k = 31, and the answer is B.
  
Answer: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  If we have k consecutive integers, then the sum of these integers is given by the formula: sum = (k/2)(2a + (k-1)d), where a is the first term and d is the common difference.
  In this problem, we know that the first term is -50, so a = -50.
  We also know that the sum is 51, so sum = 51.
  We need to find k, the number of consecutive integers.

Solution:
  We can use the formula for the sum of consecutive integers to solve for k:
  sum = (k/2)(2a + (k-1)d)
  51 = (k/2)(2(-50) + (k-1)(1))
  51 = (k/2)(-100 + k - 1)
  51 = (k/2)(k - 101)
  102 = k(k - 101)
  k^2 - 101k + 102 = 0
  (k - 1)(k - 100) = 0
  k = 1 or k = 100
  Since we are looking for a positive value of k, we can eliminate k = 1.
  Therefore, k = 100.

  The sum of k consecutive integers starting from n is given by k(n + (n+k-1))/2.
  We are given that the least integer is -50.
  We are also given that the sum of k consecutive integers is 51.
  
Action: 
  We can use the formula to set up an equation: k(-50 + (-50+k-1))/2 = 51.
  Simplifying this equation, we get: k(-99+k)/2 = 51.
  Multiplying both sides by 2, we get: k(-99+k) = 102.
  Expanding the left side, we get: -k^2 + 99k = 102.
  Rearranging, we get: k^2 - 99k + 102 = 0.
  We can solve for k using the quadratic formula: k = (99 ± sqrt(99^2 - 4(1)(102)))/2.
  Simplifying, we get: k = (99 ± sqrt(9801 - 408))/2.
  k = (99 ± sqrt(9393))/2.
  Since k must be a positive integer, we take the positive root: k = (99 + sqrt(9393))/2.
  This is approximately equal to 40.08.
  Therefore, the answer is A: 40.

Solution:
  Let's plug in the given values in the formula for the sum of k consecutive integers:
  k(-50 + (-50 + k - 1))/2 = 51
  Simplifying the equation:
  k(-99 + k)/2 = 51
  -99k/2 + k^2/2 = 51
  k^2 - 99k + 102 = 0
  Solving the quadratic equation using the quadratic formula:
  k = (99 ± sqrt(99^2 - 4*1*102))/2
  k = (99 ± sqrt(9603))/2
  k ≈ 2.46 or k ≈ 96.54
  Since k has to be a positive integer, the only possible value for k is 96.

Topic: Math
Question: A certain liquid passes through a drain at a rate of w/25 gallons every x seconds. At that rate, how many minutes will it take y gallons to pass through the drain?
Choices:
  A: y/(1200xy)
  B: 20xy/w
  C: 5xy/(12w)
  D: w/(3xy)
  E: 3y/(wx)
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  - To solve this problem, we need to use the formula: time = amount/rate
  - The rate is w/25 gallons every x seconds, which can be simplified to w/(25x) gallons per second.
  - We need to convert the time to minutes, so we need to multiply the time by 60.
Action: Answer("A")  
Using the formula, we get:
time = amount/rate
time = y/(w/(25x))
time = y * 25x/w
time = 25xy/w
Converting to minutes:
time = 25xy/w * 60/1
time = 1500xy/w
Simplifying:
time = y/(w/(25x)) * 60/1
time = y/(w/(25x)) * 60/1 * 25/25
time = y/(w/25 * x) * 1500/25
time = y/(wx) * 60 * 60/25
time = y/(wx) * 144
time = y/(1200wx/12)
time = y/(1200xy)
Therefore, the answer is A: y/(1200xy).
