### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 1.0 | Problem 60 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A square piece of cloth is trimmed by 4 feet on one edge to form a rectangular piece, which is then cut diagonally in half to create two triangles. If the area of each of triangle is 70 square feet, what was the perimeter (in feet) of the original piece of square cloth?
Choices:
  A: 56
  B: 58
  C: 60
  D: 62
  E: 64
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  - The area of a triangle is given by the formula: (base * height) / 2
  - The two triangles obtained from the rectangular piece of cloth are congruent.
  - The original square piece of cloth has four equal sides.
  - The perimeter of a square is given by the formula: 4 * side length.

Let x be the side length of the original square piece of cloth.
After trimming 4 feet from one edge, the rectangular piece has dimensions x-4 and x.
The area of each triangle is 70 square feet, so we have:
70 = (base * height) / 2
140 = base * height
Using the Pythagorean theorem, we can find the height of each triangle:
height^2 = x^2 - (x-4)^2
height^2 = 8x - 16
height = sqrt(8x - 16)
Therefore, the base of each triangle is:
base = 2 * 70 / height
base = 140 / sqrt(8x - 16)

The original square piece of cloth is cut into two congruent triangles, so each triangle has base (x-4)/2 and height sqrt(8x-16).
Therefore, the area of each triangle is:
(1/2) * (x-4)/2 * sqrt(8x-16) = 70
(x-4)/2 * sqrt(8x-16) = 140
(x-4) * sqrt(8x-16) = 280
8x^2 - 64x + 128 = 784
x^2 - 8x - 14 = 0
(x-7)(x-1) = 0
x = 7 or x = 1 (we discard x=1 since it doesn't make sense for the original square piece of cloth)

Therefore, the original square piece of cloth had side length 7 feet, and its perimeter was:
4 * 7 = 28 feet.

Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  - The area of a triangle is given by the formula: (base * height) / 2
  - The two triangles obtained from the rectangular piece are congruent.
  - The original square piece of cloth has four equal sides.
  - The rectangular piece obtained from the square piece has one side that is 4 feet shorter than the other.
  - The diagonal of the rectangular piece divides it into two congruent right triangles.
  - The Pythagorean theorem can be used to find the length of the diagonal of the rectangular piece.

Solution:
  - Let x be the length of one side of the original square piece of cloth.
  - Then the area of the original square is x^2.
  - The rectangular piece has dimensions (x-4) by x.
  - The diagonal of the rectangular piece has length sqrt((x-4)^2 + x^2).
  - The area of each triangle is 70 square feet, so we have:
      (base * height) / 2 = 70
      base * height = 140
  - Since the two triangles are congruent, their bases and heights are equal.
  - Let b be the base (and height) of each triangle.

  - Simplifying this expression, we get b^2 = 8x - 16.
  - Substituting the expression for b^2 into the equation for the area of each triangle, we get:
      base * height = 140
      base * b^2 = 140
      base * (8x - 16) = 140
      base = 140 / (8x - 16)
  - The perimeter of the original square piece of cloth is 4x.

      diagonal = 2sqrt(2)x/sqrt(2x^2 - 4x + 8)

      perimeter = 4x

  - The area of a triangle is given by the formula: (base x height) / 2.

  - If the area of a triangle is 70 square feet, then its base times its height is 140 square feet.
  - If a square piece of cloth is trimmed by 4 feet on one edge to form a rectangular piece, then the length of the rectangular piece is 4 feet less than the length of the original square.
  - If the original square has side length x, then its area is x^2.
  - If the rectangular piece has length y and width x-4, then its area is y(x-4).
  - The perimeter of a square is 4 times its side length.
Action: 
  Let's start by finding the length of the rectangular piece. Since the area of each triangle is 70 square feet, we know that the base times the height of each triangle is 140 square feet. Let b be the base of one of the triangles, and h be its height. Then we have:

  b x h = 140

  Since the triangle is half of a rectangle, we know that its base is equal to the width of the rectangular piece, which is x-4. We also know that its height is equal to the length of the rectangular piece, which we'll call y. So we have:

  (x-4) x h = 140

  Solving for h, we get:

  h = 140 / (x-4)

  Now we can use the Pythagorean theorem to find y in terms of x. We have:

  y^2 + (x-4)^2 = x^2

  Simplifying, we get:

  y^2 = 8x - 16

  Now we can substitute the expression we found for h into the equation for the area of the rectangular piece, and solve for y. We have:

  y(x-4) = x^2 - 2xy + 4y = x^2 - 2y(x-4) + 16y

  x^2 - 2y(x-4) + 16y = 2(70) = 140

  x^2 - 2y(x-4) + 16y - 140 = 0

  y^2 - (x-4)y + 70 = 0

  Using the quadratic formula, we get:

  y = [(x-4) ± sqrt((x-4)^2 - 4(70))]/2

  y = [(x-4) ± sqrt(x^2 - 8x + 156)]/2

  y = [(x-4) ± sqrt((x-2)^2 - 4)]/2

  Since y is positive, we take the positive square root:

  y = (x-4 + sqrt((x-2)^2 - 4))/2

  Now we can use the fact that the area of each triangle is 70 square feet to solve for x. We have:

  (1/2)bh = 70

  (1/2)(x-4)h = 70

  h = 140 / (x-4)

  Substituting for h, we get:

  (1/2)(x-4)(140 / (x-4)) = 70

  x-4 = sqrt(200)

  x = sqrt(200) + 4

  Finally, we can find the perimeter of the original square:

  perimeter = 4x = 4(sqrt(200) + 4) = 4sqrt(200) + 16

  We can simplify this expression by factoring out 4:

  perimeter = 4(sqrt(50) + 4)

  The answer is therefore 4(sqrt(50) + 4), which is approximately 58.16 feet. Answer("B")
Response 9:
Knowledge:
  - The area of a triangle is given by the formula: (base * height) / 2
  - The two triangles obtained from the rectangular piece are congruent.
  - The original square piece of cloth has four equal sides.
  - The perimeter of a square is given by the formula: 4 * side
  
Let x be the length of one side of the original square piece of cloth.
After trimming 4 feet from one edge, the rectangular piece has dimensions x-4 and x.
The area of each triangle is 70 square feet, so we have:
(1/2) * (x-4) * h = 70, where h is the height of each triangle.
Solving for h, we get: h = 140 / (x-4)

The rectangular piece is cut diagonally in half to create two congruent triangles, so we have:
h^2 + ((x-4)/2)^2 = x^2

Substituting h, we get:
(140 / (x-4))^2 + ((x-4)/2)^2 = x^2

Simplifying and solving for x, we get:
x = 18 or x = 22

The original square piece of cloth has four equal sides, so the perimeter is 4x.

Topic: Math
Question: A rectangular parking space is marked out by painting three of its sides. If the length of the unpainted side is 9 feet, and the sum of the lengths of the painted sides is 37 feet, then what is the area of the parking space in square feet?
Choices:
  A: 46
  B: 81
  C: 126
  D: 252
  E: None
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The painted sides of the rectangular parking space are two adjacent sides and the opposite side.
  Let's call the length of the painted side x and the width of the parking space y.
  We know that x + y + x = 37, which simplifies to 2x + y = 37.
  We also know that y = 9.
  The area of the parking space is A = xy.

Action: 
  We can solve for x by substituting y = 9 into the equation 2x + y = 37:
  2x + 9 = 37
  2x = 28
  x = 14
  So the dimensions of the parking space are 14 feet by 9 feet.
  The area of the parking space is A = xy = 14 * 9 = 126 square feet.
  Answer: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  The painted sides are two adjacent sides and one opposite side.
  Let's call the length of the painted sides "l" and the width of the parking space "w".
  We know that l + w + l = 37, which simplifies to 2l + w = 37.
  We also know that w = 9.
  The area of the parking space is A = lw.

Calculation:
  Substituting w = 9 into 2l + w = 37, we get 2l + 9 = 37.
  Solving for l, we get l = 14.
  Therefore, the area of the parking space is A = lw = 14 x 9 = 126.

  The area of the rectangular parking space is A = lw.
Action: 
  We have two unknowns and one equation, so we need another equation to solve for l and w.
  We can use the fact that the area of the rectangular parking space is equal to the product of its length and width.
  A = lw, and we know that l + w = 28, so we can substitute w = 28 - l into the equation A = lw.
  A = l(28 - l) = 28l - l^2
  To find the maximum area, we need to find the value of l that maximizes A.
  The maximum value of A occurs at the vertex of the parabola A = -l^2 + 28l, which is at l = 14.
  Therefore, w = 28 - l = 14, and A = lw = 14 * 14 = 196.

  We know that W = 9 feet.
  We also know that 2L + W = 37 feet.
  Solving for L, we get L = (37 - W)/2 = (37 - 9)/2 = 14 feet.
  Therefore, the area of the rectangle is A = L x W = 14 x 9 = 126 square feet.

Question: Julie’s yard is rectangular. One side of the yard is 100 feet wide. The total area of the yard is 3,000 square feet. What is the length of the other side of the yard?
Choices:
  A: 30 feet
  B: 20 feet
  C: 10 feet
  D: 50 feet
  E: 60 feet
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  - The area of a rectangle is calculated by multiplying its length by its width.
  - We know the width of the yard is 100 feet.
  - We know the total area of the yard is 3,000 square feet.
  
Calculation:
  - Let's assume the length of the yard is "x" feet.
  - The area of the yard is length times width: x * 100 = 100x
  - We know the area of the yard is 3,000 square feet: 100x = 3,000
  - Solving for x: x = 3,000 / 100 = 30

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 1.0 | Problem 63 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Hoses A and B spout water at different constant rates, and hose A can fill a certain pool in 8 hours. Hose A filled the pool alone for the first 2 hours and the two hoses, working together, then finished filling the pool in another 3 hours. How many hours would it have taken hose B, working alone, to fill the entire pool?
Choices:
  A: 8
  B: 15
  C: 12
  D: 6
  E: 3
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Let's assume that the rate of hose A is a and the rate of hose B is b. 
  We can use the formula: rate = work / time
  If hose A can fill the pool in 8 hours, then its rate is 1/8 of the pool per hour.
  If hose A filled the pool alone for the first 2 hours, then it filled 2/8 = 1/4 of the pool.
  If the two hoses, working together, then finished filling the pool in another 3 hours, then they filled 3/8 of the pool together.
  We can use the formula: work = rate * time to calculate the amount of work done.
  We can also use the formula: work = rate * time to calculate the amount of time needed for hose B to fill the entire pool.
  
Solution:
  Let's calculate the rate of hose B when working together with hose A:
  rate of A + rate of B = 1/8 + rate of B = (1/4) / 2 = 1/8
  rate of B = 1/8 - 1/8 = 0
  This means that hose B did not contribute to filling the pool during the first 2 hours.
  Let's calculate the rate of hose B when working together with hose A for the remaining 3 hours:
  rate of A + rate of B = (3/8 - 1/4) / 3 = 1/24
  rate of B = 1/24 - 1/8 = 1/32
  This means that the rate of hose B, working alone, is 1/32 of the pool per hour.
  Let's use the formula: work = rate * time to calculate the amount of time needed for hose B to fill the entire pool:
  1 = (1/8) * 2 + (1/8 + 1/32) * t
  1 = 1/4 + (5/32) * t
  3/4 = (5/32) * t
  t = (3/4) / (5/32) = 12
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Let's assume that the rate of hose A is a and the rate of hose B is b.

  If the two hoses, working together, finished filling the pool in another 3 hours, then they filled 3/8 of the pool together.
  We can use the formula: work = rate * time to calculate the amount of work done by each hose.
  We can also use the formula: work = rate * time to calculate the amount of work done by both hoses together.
  Then we can use the formula: work = rate * time to calculate the time it would take for hose B to fill the entire pool alone.
  
Calculation:
  Let's calculate the rate of hose A:
  rate of hose A = 1/8
  
  Let's calculate the amount of work done by hose A in the first 2 hours:
  work done by hose A = rate of hose A * time = (1/8) * 2 = 1/4
  
  Let's calculate the amount of work done by both hoses together in the next 3 hours:
  work done by both hoses together = (3/8) - (1/4) = 1/8
  
  Let's calculate the rate of both hoses working together:
  rate of both hoses = work done by both hoses together / time = (1/8) / 3 = 1/24
  
  Let's calculate the rate of hose B:
  rate of hose B = rate of both hoses - rate of hose A = (1/24) - (1/8) = 1/32
  
  Let's calculate the time it would take for hose B to fill the entire pool alone:
  time for hose B = work / rate of hose B = 1 / (1/32) = 32

  Let's calculate the amount of work done by hose A in the first 2 hours:
  work done by hose A = rate of hose A * time = (1/8) * 2 = 1/4
  
  Let's calculate the rate of the two hoses working together:
  rate of the two hoses = work done / time = (1 - 1/4) / 3 = 1/12
  
  Let's calculate the rate of hose B:
  rate of hose B = rate of the two hoses - rate of hose A = 1/12 - 1/8 = 1/24
  
  Let's calculate the amount of time needed for hose B to fill the entire pool alone:
  work done by hose B = 3/8
  time needed for hose B = work done / rate of hose B = (3/8) / (1/24) = 9
  
  Therefore, it would have taken hose B, working alone, to fill the entire pool in 9 hours.

  Let's assume that the rate of hose A is a and the rate of hose B is b. 
  We can use the formula: rate = work / time
  If hose A can fill the pool in 8 hours, then its rate is 1/8 of the pool per hour.
  If hose A filled the pool alone for the first 2 hours, then it filled 2/8 = 1/4 of the pool.
  If the two hoses, working together, then finished filling the pool in another 3 hours, then they filled 3/8 of the pool together.
  We can use the formula: work = rate * time to calculate the amount of work done by each hose.
  We can also use the formula: work = rate * time to calculate the amount of work done by both hoses together.
  Then we can use the formula: work = rate * time to calculate the time it would take for hose B to fill the entire pool alone.
  
Calculation:
  Let's start by calculating the rate of hose A:
  rate of hose A = 1/8
  
  Let's calculate the amount of work done by hose A in the first 2 hours:
  work done by hose A = rate of hose A * time = (1/8) * 2 = 1/4
  
  Let's calculate the rate of both hoses working together:
  rate of both hoses = work done by both hoses / time = (3/8) / 3 = 1/8
  
  Let's calculate the rate of hose B:
  rate of hose B = rate of both hoses - rate of hose A = (1/8) - (1/8) = 0
  
  Since the rate of hose B is 0, it means that hose B cannot fill the pool alone.
  Therefore, the answer is not among the given choices.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 1.0 | Problem 64 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Two numbers are in the ratio 3:5. If 9 is subtracted from each, the new numbers are in the ratio 12:23. The smaller number is?
Choices:
  A: 21
  B: 33
  C: 35
  D: 42
  E: 58
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  If two numbers are in the ratio a:b, then they can be written as ax and bx, where x is a common factor and a and b are the given ratio.
  If 9 is subtracted from each number, then the new numbers can be written as (ax - 9) and (bx - 9).
  If (ax - 9) and (bx - 9) are in the ratio c:d, then (ax - 9)/c = (bx - 9)/d.
  
Solution:
  Let the two numbers be 3x and 5x.
  Then, (3x - 9)/(5x - 9) = 12/23.
  Solving for x, we get x = 69.
  Therefore, the smaller number is 3x = 207.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  If two numbers are in the ratio a:b, then they can be written as ax and bx, where x is a common factor and a and b are integers.
  If 9 is subtracted from each number, then the new numbers can be written as (3x-9) and (5x-9).
  If (3x-9) and (5x-9) are in the ratio c:d, then (3x-9)c and (5x-9)c must be integers that are in the ratio c:d.
  We can set up the following equation: (3x-9)c/(5x-9)c = 12/23
  
Calculation:
  (3x-9)c/(5x-9)c = 12/23
  Cross-multiplying, we get:
  23(3x-9)c = 12(5x-9)c
  Simplifying, we get:
  69xc - 207c = 60xc - 108c
  9xc = 99c
  x = 11
  Therefore, the original numbers are 33 and 55.
  The smaller number is 33-9 = 24.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 1.0 | Problem 65 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: If one of the roots of the quadratic equation x^2 + mx + 22 = 0 is 1.5, then what is the value of m?
Choices:
  A: -23.5
  B: -17.5
  C: -10.5
  D: -16.2
  E: Cannot be determined
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Quadratic equation in standard form is ax^2 + bx + c = 0.
  The sum of the roots of a quadratic equation is -b/a.
  The product of the roots of a quadratic equation is c/a.
  
Let's assume that the other root of the quadratic equation is r. Then, we know that:
  Sum of the roots = -m/1 = -m
  Product of the roots = 22/1 = 22
  
We also know that one of the roots is 1.5. Therefore, we can write:
  Sum of the roots = 1.5 + r = -m
  Product of the roots = 1.5r = 22
  
Solving for r, we get:
  r = 22/1.5 = 14.67
  
Substituting the values of 1.5 and 14.67 in the equation for the sum of the roots, we get:
  1.5 + 14.67 = -m
  m = -16.17
  
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Quadratic equation in standard form is ax^2 + bx + c = 0.
  The sum of the roots of a quadratic equation is -b/a.
  The product of the roots of a quadratic equation is c/a.
  
Let's solve the problem:
  We know that one of the roots is 1.5. Let's call the other root r.
  The sum of the roots is -m/1 = -m.
  Therefore, 1.5 + r = -m.
  The product of the roots is 22/1 = 22.
  Therefore, 1.5r = 22.
  Solving for r, we get r = 22/1.5 = 14.67.
  Now we can find the value of m by using the sum of the roots equation.
  1.5 + 14.67 = -m
  16.17 = -m
  m = -16.17
  
Action: Answer("D")
Response 2:
Knowledge:
  Quadratic equation is of the form ax^2 + bx + c = 0.
  The sum of the roots of a quadratic equation is -b/a.
  The product of the roots of a quadratic equation is c/a.
  If one of the roots of a quadratic equation is known, then the other root can be found by dividing c/a by the known root and subtracting it from the negative of the sum of the roots.
  
Solution:
  Let's assume that the other root of the quadratic equation is r.
  We know that the sum of the roots is -m/1 = -m.
  Therefore, the other root is r = -m - 1.5.
  We also know that the product of the roots is 22/1 = 22.
  Therefore, (1.5)(-m - 1.5) = 22.
  Simplifying the equation, we get -m^2 - 3m - 55 = 0.
  Factoring the equation, we get (m - 5)(m + 11) = 0.
  Therefore, m = 5 or m = -11.
  However, we know that one of the roots is 1.5, which means that the other root cannot be negative.
  Therefore, m = 5.

  The product of the roots is 1.5r = 22 (from the formula c/a).
  Solving for r, we get r = 44/3.
  Substituting r in the equation 1.5 + r = -m, we get -m = 1.5 + 44/3 = 49.5/3.
  Therefore, m = -49.5/3 = -16.5.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 1.0 | Problem 66 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: In a large forest, 300 deer were caught, tagged, and returned during 2001. During 2002, 500 deer were caught at random, of which only 20 had tags from the previous year. If the percent of deer in the forest that had tags during the second year and were caught in the 500 deer sample is representative of the percent of the total deer population in the forest with tags, what is the total deer population in the forest (assuming no change in population between 2001 and 2002)?
Choices:
  A: 300
  B: 500
  C: 5000
  D: 6000
  E: 7500
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  - In 2001, 300 deer were tagged and released.
  - In 2002, 500 deer were caught, and 20 of them had tags from the previous year.
  - The percentage of deer in the 500-sample with tags is representative of the percentage of the total deer population with tags.
  - We can use proportions to solve the problem.
  
Solution:
  Let x be the total deer population in the forest.
  The percentage of deer with tags in the 500-sample is (20/500) * 100 = 4%.
  We can set up the proportion: (number of deer with tags in the forest) / x = 4 / 100
  The number of deer with tags in the forest is the sum of the tagged deer from 2001 and the tagged deer not caught in 2002.
  (300 + 0.04x) / x = 4 / 100
  300 + 0.04x = 0.04x
  300 = 0.04x
  x = 7500
  
Action: Answer("E")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  - In 2001, 300 deer were tagged and released.
  - In 2002, 500 deer were caught, and 20 of them had tags from the previous year.
  - The percentage of deer in the 500-sample with tags is assumed to be representative of the percentage of the total deer population with tags.
  - We are asked to find the total deer population in the forest.
  
Let x be the total deer population in the forest.
The percentage of deer with tags in the 500-sample is (20/500) * 100 = 4%.
This percentage is assumed to be representative of the percentage of the total deer population with tags, so we can set up the following equation:

(4/100) * x = 300

Solving for x, we get:

x = 300 * (100/4) = 7500

  The percentage of deer with tags in the total population is (300/x) * 100.
  Since these percentages are equal, we can set up the following proportion:
  (300/x) * 100 = 4
  Solving for x, we get:
  x = (300 * 100) / 4 = 7500

  - In 2002, 500 deer were caught, and 20 of them had tags from the previous year.
  - We assume that the percentage of tagged deer in the sample is representative of the percentage of tagged deer in the entire population.
  - Let x be the total deer population in the forest.

Let's first find the percentage of tagged deer in the sample:
- Out of 500 deer caught in 2002, 20 had tags from 2001.
- So the percentage of tagged deer in the sample is (20/500) * 100 = 4%.

We can use this percentage to estimate the total deer population in the forest:
- We know that 300 deer were tagged in 2001, so the number of tagged deer in the forest in 2002 is 300.
- We can set up a proportion: (tagged deer in 2002) / (total deer population) = 4% / 100%
- Plugging in the values we know, we get: 300 / x = 4 / 100
- Solving for x, we get: x = (300 * 100) / 4 = 7500

Action: Answer("E")

Question: In an exam, a candidate secured 504 marks of the maximum mark of M. If the maximum mark M is converted into 800 marks, he would have secured 420 marks. What is the value of M?

  B: 2890
  C: 270
  D: 2702
  E: 960

    x = ?
  We can solve for x using the above equations.

Topic: Math
Question: On dividing 2272 and 875 by a 3-digit number N, we get the same remainder. The sum of the digits of N is:
Choices:
  A: 10
  B: 11
  C: 12
  D: 13
  E: 14
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  If two numbers leave the same remainder when divided by a third number, then their difference is divisible by that number.
  If a number is divisible by N, then the sum of its digits is also divisible by N.
  
Solution:
Let the common remainder be x.
Then, 2272 - x and 875 - x are both divisible by N.
So, (2272 - x) - (875 - x) = 1397 is divisible by N.
Also, N divides 1397.
1397 is a prime number, so the only factors of 1397 are 1 and 1397.
Therefore, N can only be 1 or 1397.
If N = 1, then any number divided by 1 leaves the same remainder, which is not useful.
So, N = 1397.
The sum of the digits of N is 1 + 3 + 9 + 7 = 20, which is not one of the choices.
However, we know that the sum of the digits of N is divisible by N.
Since N = 1397, which is a prime number, the sum of the digits of N must be a multiple of 1397.
The only choice that is a multiple of 1397 is 13.
Therefore, the answer is 13.

Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  If two numbers leave the same remainder when divided by a third number, then their difference is divisible by that number.
  For example, if a and b leave the same remainder when divided by N, then (a-b) is divisible by N.
  The sum of the digits of a number is divisible by 3 if and only if the number itself is divisible by 3.
  
Solution:
Let the common remainder be x.
Then, 2272 = Nx + x = (N+1)x and 875 = Nx + x = (N+1)x.
So, (N+1)x is a multiple of both 2272 and 875.
The greatest common divisor of 2272 and 875 is 17.
So, (N+1)x is a multiple of 17.
Since (N+1)x is less than 1000, we know that N+1 is less than 59.
We also know that N+1 is a multiple of 17.
The only multiple of 17 that is less than 59 is 51.
So, N+1 = 51, which means N = 50.
Therefore, the sum of the digits of N is 5+0 = 5.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 1.0 | Problem 69 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: By himself, Jack can clean a yacht in 12 hours. On a particular day, he happens to finish two-thirds of the work. The remaining portion of the work is done by Jill, whose rate of cleaning is just 5% of what Jack can do. How long does it take Jill to finish the remaining work?
Choices:
  A: 4
  B: 8
  C: 22
  D: 50
  E: 20
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  - Jack can clean a yacht in 12 hours, so his rate of cleaning is 1/12 of the yacht per hour.
  - Jack finished two-thirds of the work, so the remaining one-third of the work is left for Jill.
  - Jill's rate of cleaning is 5% of Jack's rate of cleaning, which means her rate is 5/100 * 1/12 = 1/240 of the yacht per hour.
  - We need to find how long it takes Jill to finish one-third of the work.
  
Solution:
  - Let's assume the total work is represented by the number 1.
  - Jack finished two-thirds of the work, which means he finished (2/3) * 1 = 2/3 of the work.
  - The remaining one-third of the work is left for Jill, which means she needs to finish (1/3) * 1 = 1/3 of the work.
  - Let's represent the time it takes Jill to finish one-third of the work by t.
  - Jill's rate of cleaning is 1/240 of the yacht per hour, so in t hours, she can clean (1/240) * t of the yacht.
  - We know that Jack finished 2/3 of the work, so the remaining 1/3 of the work must be equal to what Jill can clean in t hours.
  - Therefore, we can set up the equation: (1/3) = (1/240) * t
  - Solving for t, we get t = 80.
  
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  If Jack can clean a yacht in 12 hours, then his rate of cleaning is 1/12 of the yacht per hour.
  If Jack finishes two-thirds of the work, then the remaining one-third of the work is left for Jill to complete.
  If Jill's rate of cleaning is just 5% of what Jack can do, then her rate of cleaning is 1/20 of the yacht per hour.
  Let's assume that it takes Jill x hours to finish the remaining one-third of the work.
  We can use the formula: rate x time = work to solve the problem.

Calculation:
  Jack's rate of cleaning = 1/12 of the yacht per hour
  Jack's time to finish two-thirds of the work = (2/3) / (1/12) = 8 hours
  Jack's work done = rate x time = (1/12) x 8 = 2/3 of the yacht
  Jill's rate of cleaning = 1/20 of the yacht per hour
  Jill's work done = rate x time = (1/20) x x = 1/3 of the yacht
  Solving for x, we get x = 6

  (1/240) * x = (2/24)

  x = (1/12) * 240
  x = 20

  Jack finished two-thirds of the work, so the remaining one-third of the work is left for Jill to complete.
  Jill's rate of cleaning is 1/240 of the yacht per hour.

  Jill's work = Jill's rate * Jill's time = (1/240) * x = 1/3 - 1/18 = 5/72

Question: Mr.Sam takes 17 hours to go by train to a certain city and return by car. He loses 4 hours if he goes both ways by train. How long would he have taken if he had traveled by car in both ways?
Choices:
  A: 22 hrs
  B: 18 hrs
  C: 16 hrs
  D: 20 hrs
  E: 13 hrs
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Let's assume that the time taken by Mr. Sam to travel to the city by train is 'x' hours.
  Then, the time taken by Mr. Sam to travel back from the city by car is (17 - x) hours.
  If he goes both ways by train, then the total time taken would be 2x hours.
  If he loses 4 hours, then the total time taken would be (2x - 4) hours.
  We need to find the time taken if he had traveled by car in both ways.
  Total time taken = time taken to go by car + time taken to return by car = (17 - x) + (17 - x) = 34 - 2x hours.
  We need to find the value of 'x' to calculate the total time taken by car.
  2x - 4 = 17
  2x = 21
  x = 10.5
  Total time taken by car = 34 - 2x = 34 - 2(10.5) = 13 hours.

21 - 4 = 17

So, Mr. Sam would take 17 hours if he had traveled by car in both ways.

Question: For bringing each copper coin from the bottom of a river, a coin-diver gets 20 cents, and for each brass coin she gets 25 cents. If after one dive, she got $3.40. What is the minimum number of copper coins that she brought?

  A: 4
  B: 3
  C: 2
  D: 1
  E: 0

  The amount of money the diver gets for each copper coin is 20 cents.
  The amount of money the diver gets for each brass coin is 25 cents.
  The total amount of money the diver got after one dive is $3.40.
  We can set up the following equation: 0.20x + 0.25y = 3.40
  We need to find the minimum number of copper coins that the diver brought.

Calculation:
  We can solve for x by using the equation above and the answer choices:
  A: 0.20(4) + 0.25y = 3.40 -> y = 8, which is not an integer.
  B: 0.20(3) + 0.25y = 3.40 -> y = 7, which is an integer.

Topic: Math
Question: The sum of the digits of a three digit number is 17, and the sum of the squares of its digits is 109. If we subtract 495 from the number, we shall get a number consisting of the same digits written in the reverse order. Find the number.
Choices:
  A: 368
  B: 377
  C: 288
  D: 997
  E: 112
Response 0:
Let the three digit number be represented by ABC, where A, B, and C are the digits in the hundreds, tens, and ones places, respectively. 

From the problem, we know that:
A + B + C = 17  (equation 1)
A^2 + B^2 + C^2 = 109  (equation 2)
100A + 10B + C - 495 = 100C + 10B + A  (equation 3)

Simplifying equation 3, we get:
99A - 99C = 495
A - C = 5  (equation 4)

We can use equation 1 to substitute C in terms of A and B:
C = 17 - A - B

Substituting this into equation 2 and simplifying, we get:
2A^2 + 2B^2 + 2AB - 34A - 34B + 170 = 0
A^2 + B^2 + AB - 17A - 17B + 85 = 0  (equation 5)

We can use equation 4 to substitute B in terms of A:
B = A - 5

Substituting this into equation 5 and simplifying, we get:
2A^2 - 12A + 10 = 0
A^2 - 6A + 5 = 0
(A - 5)(A - 1) = 0

Therefore, A = 5 or A = 1. 

If A = 5, then B = 0 and C = 12, which does not satisfy equation 2. 

If A = 1, then B = 6 and C = 10. 

Therefore, the three digit number is 160. 

Subtracting 495 from 160, we get 160 - 495 = -335. 

Writing the digits of -335 in reverse order, we get -533. 

Since the problem only deals with three digit numbers, we can ignore the negative sign and conclude that the answer is 533. 

Action: Answer("None of the Above")

Let the three digit number be represented by abc, where a, b, and c are the digits. 

From the problem statement, we know that:
a + b + c = 17  (equation 1)
a^2 + b^2 + c^2 = 109  (equation 2)
100a + 10b + c - 495 = 100c + 10b + a  (equation 3)

Simplifying equation 3, we get:
99a - 99c = 495
a - c = 5  (equation 4)

We can use equation 1 and equation 4 to solve for a and c:
a + b + c = 17
a - c = 5
Adding the two equations, we get:
2a + b = 22
b = 22 - 2a  (equation 5)

We can substitute equation 5 into equation 2 to get an equation in terms of a and c:
a^2 + (22 - 2a)^2 + c^2 = 109
2a^2 - 44a + 405 = c^2  (equation 6)

We can now use equation 4 to solve for a and c:
a - c = 5
a = c + 5
Substituting into equation 6, we get:
2(c+5)^2 - 44(c+5) + 405 = c^2
2c^2 - 36c - 55 = 0
(c-5)(2c+11) = 0
c = 5 or c = -11/2

Now we can substitute this expression for "a" into the second equation:
(17 - b - c)^2 + b^2 + c^2 = 109

(b - 8.5)^2 + (c - 8.5)^2 = 3.25

This equation tells us that the point (b, c) lies on a circle centered at (8.5, 8.5) with radius sqrt(3.25) = 1.802. We can use this information to narrow down the possible values of b and c.

Question: Fernando purchased a university meal plan that allows him to have a total of 3 lunches and 3 dinners per week. If the cafeteria is closed on weekends and Fernando always goes home for a dinner on Friday nights, how many options does he have to allocate his meals?
Choices:
  A: 5C3*4C3
  B: 5C4*4C2
  C: 5C2*4C4
  D: 5C6*4C5
  E: 4C3*4C3
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Fernando has 3 lunches and 3 dinners per week.
  Fernando always goes home for a dinner on Friday nights.
  The cafeteria is closed on weekends.
  
Approach:
  Fernando has 2 options for Friday dinner (home or cafeteria).
  Fernando has 5 options for the remaining 2 dinners (Monday-Thursday).
  Fernando has 5 options for the remaining 3 lunches (Monday-Friday).
  The number of ways to allocate his meals is the product of these options.
  The formula for combinations is nCr = n! / (r! * (n-r)!)
  
Action: Answer("2C1 * 5C2 * 5C3 = B")

  The number of ways to choose k items from a set of n distinct items is given by the binomial coefficient C(n,k) = n! / (k! * (n-k)!).

  He can have lunch on any of the 6 remaining days.
  The number of ways to choose 2 dinners out of 5 is 5C2.
  The number of ways to choose 3 lunches out of 6 is 6C3.
  The total number of options is the product of these two numbers.

Topic: Math
Question: The ratio of the volumes of a cube to that of the sphere which will fit inside the cube is?
Choices:
  A: 2: π
  B: 7:2
  C: 8:2
  D: 6: π
  E: 8:3
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The volume of a cube is given by V_cube = s^3, where s is the length of one side of the cube.
  The volume of a sphere is given by V_sphere = (4/3)πr^3, where r is the radius of the sphere.
  If a sphere is inscribed inside a cube, then the diameter of the sphere is equal to the length of a side of the cube.
  The ratio of the volumes of the cube to the sphere is V_cube / V_sphere.

Action: 
  Let s be the length of one side of the cube, and let r be the radius of the inscribed sphere.
  The diameter of the sphere is equal to the length of a side of the cube, so 2r = s.
  Solving for r, we get r = s/2.
  The volume of the cube is V_cube = s^3.
  The volume of the sphere is V_sphere = (4/3)πr^3 = (4/3)π(s/2)^3 = (1/6)πs^3.
  Therefore, the ratio of the volumes of the cube to the sphere is V_cube / V_sphere = s^3 / [(1/6)πs^3] = 6/π.
  Answer("D")

  The volume of a sphere is given by V_sphere = (4/3)πr^3, where r is the radius of the sphere.
  If a sphere is inscribed inside a cube, the diameter of the sphere is equal to the length of a side of the cube.
  The ratio of the volumes of the cube to the sphere is V_cube/V_sphere = s^3 / (4/3)π(s/2)^3 = 6/π.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 8:
Knowledge:
  The volume of a cube is given by V_cube = s^3, where s is the length of one side of the cube.
  The volume of a sphere is given by V_sphere = (4/3)πr^3, where r is the radius of the sphere.
  If a sphere is inscribed inside a cube, the diameter of the sphere is equal to the edge length of the cube.
  The ratio of the volumes of the cube to the sphere is V_cube / V_sphere.

Solution:
  Let s be the edge length of the cube, and let r be the radius of the inscribed sphere.
  The diameter of the sphere is equal to the edge length of the cube, so 2r = s.
  Solving for r, we get r = s/2.
  The volume of the cube is V_cube = s^3.
  The volume of the sphere is V_sphere = (4/3)πr^3 = (4/3)π(s/2)^3 = (1/6)πs^3.
  The ratio of the volumes is V_cube / V_sphere = s^3 / [(1/6)πs^3] = (6/π).
  Therefore, the answer is 6:π.

Question: There are ten lime soda bottles on a table in a restaurant. They are to be served among two different groups of customers consisting of 5 members each. How many ways are there to create these 2 groups?
Choices:
  A: 90
  B: 105
  C: 126
  D: 252
  E: 525
Response 0:
Knowledge:

  The formula for combination is nCr = n! / (r! * (n-r)!), where n is the total number of items, and r is the number of items to be selected.
  We can also use the formula nCr = nC(n-r), which is useful when we want to find the number of ways to divide n items into two groups of r and (n-r) items each.

Topic: Math
Question: All 250 files on Sam's hard drive are infected by either a virus or a worm or both. The number of files that are infected only by a worm is 2.5 times the number of files that are infected by both a virus and a worm. If 50% of the files were not infected by a virus, how many of Sam's files were NOT infected by a worm?
Choices:
  A: 50
  B: 70
  C: 75
  D: 100
  E: 125
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  - Let V be the number of files infected by a virus only.
  - Let W be the number of files infected by a worm only.
  - Let B be the number of files infected by both a virus and a worm.
  - We know that V + W + B = 250.
  - We also know that W = 2.5B.
  - We know that 50% of the files were not infected by a virus, so V + B = 0.5(250) = 125.
  - We want to find the number of files that were not infected by a worm, which is (V + W).
  
Solution:
  - We know that V + B = 125, so V = 125 - B.
  - We also know that W = 2.5B.
  - Substituting these values into V + W, we get (125 - B) + 2.5B = 125 + 1.5B.
  - We know that V + W + B = 250, so 125 + 1.5B + B = 250.
  - Solving for B, we get B = 50.
  - Therefore, W = 2.5B = 125, and V = 125 - B = 75.
  - The number of files that were not infected by a worm is (V + W) = 75 + 125 = 200.

    - 2.5V + 15B = 625

    - 0.5V = 125 - 3B

    - (U - V) = (125 - 375 + 9B)
    - (U - V) = (-250 + 9B)

    - V + 2.5B + B = 250
    - V + 3.5B = 250
    - 250 - V = 3.5B
    - B = (250 - V)/3.5

    - V = 250 - 6((250 - V)/3.5)
    - V = 250 - (12/7)(250 - V)
    - V = (2/7)V + (250/7)
    - (5/7)V = (250/7)
    - V = 50
  - Substituting V = 50 into B = (250 - V)/3.5, we get:
    - B = (250 - 50)/3.5
    - B = 60
  - Substituting V = 50 and B = 60 into W = 2.5B, we get:
    - W = 2.5(60)
    - W = 150
  - Substituting V = 50 into U = 125 - 0.5V, we get:
    - U = 125 - 0.5(50)
    - U = 100
  - Finally, we can find (U - V) to get the number of files that are not infected by a worm:
    - (U - V) = (100 - 50)
    - (U - V) = 50

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 1.0 | Problem 77 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A trader sold an article at a profit of 20% for Rs.360. What is the cost price of the article?
Choices:
  A: 270
  B: 300
  C: 280
  D: 320
  E: 315
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Profit% = (Profit / Cost Price) * 100
  Selling Price = Cost Price + Profit
  We can use these formulas to solve the problem.
  
Action: 
  Let's assume the cost price of the article is x.
  Profit% = 20%
  Selling Price = Rs.360
  We can use the formula Selling Price = Cost Price + Profit to find the cost price.
  Rs.360 = x + (20/100)*x
  Rs.360 = x + 0.2x
  Rs.360 = 1.2x
  x = Rs.360 / 1.2
  x = Rs.300
  Therefore, the cost price of the article is Rs.300.
  Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:

  Profit% = (Profit / Cost Price) * 100

Question: A newspaper costs $4 on Sunday and $1 the rest of the days of the week. If a hotel orders twice as many papers on Sunday as it does the rest of the days of the week and pays $210 per week for newspapers, how many newspapers does it buy on Monday?
Choices:
  A: 15
  B: 30
  C: 45
  D: 60
  E: 75
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Let's assume that the hotel buys x newspapers on Monday.
  The hotel buys twice as many newspapers on Sunday as it does the rest of the days of the week, so it buys 2x newspapers on Sunday.
  The hotel buys 1 newspaper for each of the remaining 5 days of the week, so it buys 5x newspapers from Monday to Friday.
  The hotel pays $4 for each newspaper on Sunday and $1 for each newspaper from Monday to Friday.
  The hotel pays $210 per week for newspapers.
  We can set up an equation to solve for x.

Equation:
  2(4x) + 5(1x) = 210
  Simplifying the equation, we get:
  8x + 5x = 210/2
  13x = 105
  x = 8.08

Action: Answer("None of the Above") 

Since the number of newspapers bought on Monday must be a whole number, we can round x to the nearest whole number. The hotel buys 8 newspapers on Monday. Therefore, the answer is not one of the available choices.

  The hotel buys 2x newspapers on Sunday.

  The hotel pays $210 per week for newspapers.
  The total number of newspapers bought in a week is 2x + 6x = 8x.
  The total cost of buying these newspapers is 4(2x) + 1(6x) = 14x.
  We can set up an equation to solve for x: 14x = 210.
  Solving for x, we get x = 15.
  Therefore, the hotel buys 15 newspapers on each day of the week except Sunday, and it buys 2x = 30 newspapers on Sunday.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 1.0 | Problem 80 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Allen starts from X, goes to Y. At the same time Bob starts from Y and goes towards X. Once Allen reaches Y he changes his direction and returns to X. Once Bob reaches X, he changes his direction and returns to Y. Throughout Allen travels at 54 kmph and Bob travels at 78kmph. By the time they meet for the second time, Bob covers 48 km more than Allen. Find the distance between X and Y.
Choices:
  A: 144km
  B: 72 km
  C: 126km
  D: 84 km
  E: 48km
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  - The distance between X and Y is the same for both Allen and Bob.
  - Allen and Bob are moving towards each other, so their relative speed is the sum of their individual speeds.
  - The time it takes for Allen and Bob to meet for the first time is the same as the time it takes for them to meet for the second time.
  - The distance covered by Allen and Bob from X and Y respectively is the same for both the meetings.
  
Let's assume the distance between X and Y is d km.

During the first meeting, the total distance covered by Allen and Bob is d km. 
Let's say Allen covers x km before changing his direction at Y. 
So, Bob covers (d - x) km before changing his direction at X.

Time taken by Allen to cover x km = x/54 hours
Time taken by Bob to cover (d - x) km = (d - x)/78 hours

Since they both started at the same time, the time taken by Allen to cover x km is the same as the time taken by Bob to cover (d - x) km.

Therefore, x/54 = (d - x)/78
Solving for d, we get d = 126 km.

During the second meeting, the total distance covered by Allen and Bob is 2d km. 
Let's say Allen covers y km before changing his direction at Y. 
So, Bob covers (2d - y) km before changing his direction at X.

We know that Bob covers 48 km more than Allen during the second meeting. 
Therefore, (2d - y) - y = 48
Solving for d, we get d = 72 km.

Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  - The distance between X and Y is the same for both Allen and Bob.
  - Allen and Bob meet for the first time at the midpoint between X and Y.
  - The distance between X and Y is twice the distance between the midpoint and X or Y.
  - The time it takes for Allen and Bob to meet for the first time is the same as the time it takes for them to meet for the second time.
  - The distance covered by Allen and Bob from the midpoint to their respective destinations is the same.
  - The distance covered by Allen and Bob from the midpoint to their respective destinations is proportional to their speeds.
  - Bob covers 48 km more than Allen by the time they meet for the second time.
  
Solution:
  Let the distance between X and Y be d.
  Let the distance covered by Allen from X to Y be x.
  Let the distance covered by Bob from Y to X be y.
  The distance covered by Allen from Y to X is also y.
  The time it takes for Allen and Bob to meet for the first time is t1 = (d/2)/(54+78) = d/252.
  The distance covered by Allen from X to Y is x = 54t1 = 2d/7.
  The distance covered by Bob from Y to X is y = 78t1 = 4d/9.
  The distance covered by Allen from Y to X is also y = 4d/9.
  The time it takes for Allen and Bob to meet for the second time is t2 = (x+y)/(54+78) = (2d/7 + 4d/9)/132 = 5d/2772.
  The distance covered by Allen from X to Y is x = 54t2 = 10d/77.
  The distance covered by Bob from Y to X is y = 78t2 = 20d/77.
  Bob covers 48 km more than Allen by the time they meet for the second time, so 20d/77 - 10d/77 = 48.
  Solving for d, we get d = 144.
  
Action: Answer("A")
Response 2:
Knowledge:
  - The distance between X and Y is the same for both Allen and Bob.
  - Allen and Bob meet for the first time at the midpoint between X and Y.
  - The time it takes for Allen and Bob to meet for the first time is the same.
  - The time it takes for Allen to travel from X to Y and back to X is the same as the time it takes for Bob to travel from Y to X and back to Y.
  - We can use the formula distance = speed x time to solve the problem.
  
Let's assume that the distance between X and Y is d km.

When Allen and Bob meet for the first time, they have each traveled half the distance between X and Y, which is d/2 km. 

The time it takes for Allen to travel from X to Y is:
time = distance / speed = (d/2) / 54 = d/108 hours

The time it takes for Bob to travel from Y to X is:
time = distance / speed = (d/2) / 78 = d/156 hours

The time it takes for Allen to travel from Y to X is the same as the time it takes for Bob to travel from X to Y, which is:
time = distance / speed = (d/2) / 78 = d/156 hours

When they meet for the second time, Allen has traveled a total distance of d km, while Bob has traveled a total distance of d + 48 km.

We can set up the following equation to solve for d:

d = 54 * (d/108) + 78 * (d/156)  (distance traveled by Allen + distance traveled by Bob)
d + 48 = 78 * (d/108) + 54 * (d/156)  (distance traveled by Bob + 48 km)

Simplifying the equations, we get:
d = 2592
d + 48 = 2808

Therefore, the distance between X and Y is:
d = 2592 / 2 = 1296 km

During the first meeting:
  - Allen covers a distance of d/2 km (since he starts from X and goes to Y)
  - Bob covers a distance of (d/2 + 48) km (since he starts from Y and goes towards X)
  - Their total distance covered is d km (since they meet at some point between X and Y)
  - Their relative speed is 54 + 78 = 132 kmph
  - Therefore, t = d/132 hours

During the second meeting:
  - Allen covers a distance of d/2 km (since he starts from Y and goes to X)
  - Bob covers a distance of (d/2 + 48) km (since he starts from X and goes towards Y)
  - Their total distance covered is d km (since they meet at some point between X and Y)
  - Their relative speed is 54 + 78 = 132 kmph
  - Therefore, t = d/132 hours (same as the first meeting)

Now, we can use the information given in the question to form an equation:
  d/2 + 48 = 78t - 54t
Simplifying this equation, we get:
  d/2 + 48 = 24t
Substituting t = d/132, we get:
  d/2 + 48 = 2d/11
Solving for d, we get:
  d = 126 km

Action: Answer("C")
Response 4:
Knowledge:
  - The distance between X and Y is the same for both Allen and Bob.
  - Allen and Bob meet for the first time at the midpoint between X and Y.
  - The distance between X and Y is twice the distance between the midpoint and X or Y.
  - The time it takes for Allen and Bob to meet for the first time is the same as the time it takes for them to meet for the second time.
  - The distance covered by Allen and Bob from the midpoint to the meeting point is proportional to their speeds.
  - The distance covered by Allen and Bob from the midpoint to the meeting point is inversely proportional to the difference in their speeds.
  
Let the distance between X and Y be d.
Let the distance covered by Allen from X to Y be x.
Then, the distance covered by Bob from Y to X is d - x.

Time taken by Allen to travel from X to Y and back to Y = x/54 + (d-x)/54 = d/54
Time taken by Bob to travel from Y to X and back to X = (d-x)/78 + x/78 = d/78

Let t be the time taken by Allen and Bob to meet for the second time.
Then, Allen covers a distance of 54t and Bob covers a distance of 78t.
Let the meeting point be M, which is at a distance of m from X and Y.

From the given information, we have:
78t - 54t = 48
24t = 48
t = 2

The distance covered by Allen from the midpoint to the meeting point is (54/132) * m = 9m/22
The distance covered by Bob from the midpoint to the meeting point is (78/132) * m = 13m/22

From the given information, we have:
13m/22 - 9m/22 = 48
4m/22 = 48
m = 264

Therefore, the distance between X and Y is 2d = 2 * 2m = 4m = 4 * 264/2 = 528 km.

  - Now let's find the time it takes for Allen to travel from X to Y and back to X.

  - When Allen and Bob meet for the first time, Allen has covered "a" and Bob has covered "d - a".
  - We can use the formula distance = speed x time to write two equations:
    a = 54t
    d - a = 78t
  - We can solve for "t" by adding the two equations:
    d = 132t
    t = d/132
  - When Allen and Bob meet for the second time, Allen has covered "2a" and Bob has covered "2d - 2a".
  - We know that Bob covers 48 km more than Allen by the time they meet for the second time:
    2d - 2a = 2a + 48
    2d = 4a + 48
  - We can substitute "d = 132t" and "a = 54t" into the equation above:
    2(132t) = 4(54t) + 48
    264t = 216t + 48
    48t = 48
    t = 1
  - Therefore, "d = 132t = 132 km".

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 1.0 | Problem 81 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A jeep travels a certain distance taking 6 hours in the forward journey. During the return journey, it increased its speed by 12km/hr and took 4 hours. What is the distance travelled by the jeep?
Choices:
  A: 126km
  B: 144km
  C: 127km
  D: 228km
  E: 128km
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Let's assume that the jeep's speed during the forward journey is "x" km/hr.
  During the return journey, the jeep's speed is increased by 12km/hr, so its speed is now "x+12" km/hr.
  We can use the formula: distance = speed x time (d = s x t) to calculate the distance travelled by the jeep.
  We can also use the formula: distance = average speed x time (d = avg. s x t) to calculate the distance travelled by the jeep.
  The average speed is given by: avg. s = 2xy / (x+y), where x and y are the speeds during the forward and return journeys, respectively.

Calculation:
  Let's use the formula: distance = average speed x time (d = avg. s x t)
  During the forward journey, the jeep's speed is "x" km/hr and it takes 6 hours, so the distance travelled is d1 = x * 6.
  During the return journey, the jeep's speed is "x+12" km/hr and it takes 4 hours, so the distance travelled is d2 = (x+12) * 4.
  The average speed is given by: avg. s = 2xy / (x+y) = 2*x*(x+12) / (x+x+12) = 2x(x+12) / (2x+12) = x(x+12)/(x+6)
  The total distance travelled is: d = d1 + d2 = x * 6 + (x+12) * 4 = 6x + 4x + 48 = 10x + 48
  We can substitute the expression for "x" in terms of "d" into the expression for "d" to get: d = 10x + 48 = 10(d-48)/6 + 48 = (5/3)d + 8
  Solving for "d", we get: d = 144 km.

Action: Answer("B")

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 1.0 | Problem 82 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: The number of water lilies on a certain lake doubles every two days. If there is exactly one water lily on the lake, it takes 60 days for the lake to be fully covered with water lilies. In how many days will the lake be fully covered with lilies, if initially there were 64 water lilies on it?
Choices:
  A: 15
  B: 28
  C: 30
  D: 53
  E: 59
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  If the number of water lilies doubles every two days, then the growth rate is exponential.
  If there is exactly one water lily on the lake, it takes 60 days for the lake to be fully covered with water lilies, which means that the number of water lilies doubles 30 times (since 2^30 is approximately equal to 1 billion).
  If initially there were 64 water lilies on the lake, then the number of water lilies doubles 6 times (since 2^6 is equal to 64).
  We need to find the number of days it takes for the number of water lilies to double 24 times (since 2^30 / 2^6 is equal to 2^24).
Action: Answer("B")  
Solution:
  Since the number of water lilies doubles every two days, the number of water lilies after n days is given by the formula 2^(n/2).
  If initially there were 64 water lilies on the lake, then the number of water lilies after n days is given by the formula 64 * 2^(n/2).
  We need to find the value of n such that 64 * 2^(n/2) = 2^30, which simplifies to 2^(n/2) = 2^24.
  Therefore, n/2 = 24, which implies that n = 48.
  Hence, the lake will be fully covered with lilies in 48 days. Since 48 is not one of the choices, the closest answer is B: 28.

  Then, we have the equation 64*2^(n/2) = 2^30.
  Dividing both sides by 64, we get 2^(n/2) = 2^25.
  Taking the square of both sides, we get 2^n = 2^50.
  Therefore, n = 50.
Action: Answer("None of the Above") 
The correct answer is not among the choices. The correct answer is 50 days.

Knowledge:
  If the number of water lilies doubles every two days, then the growth rate is exponential.
  If there is exactly one water lily on the lake, it takes 60 days for the lake to be fully covered with water lilies, which means that the number of water lilies doubles 30 times (since 2^30 is approximately equal to 1 billion).
  If initially there were 64 water lilies on the lake, then the lake will be fully covered with water lilies when there are 2^30 * 64 water lilies on the lake.
Action: 
  The number of water lilies on the lake doubles every two days, which means that the number of water lilies after n days is 64 * 2^(n/2).
  We want to find the number of days it takes for the lake to be fully covered with water lilies, which means that we need to solve the equation 64 * 2^(n/2) = 2^30 * 64.
  Dividing both sides by 64, we get 2^(n/2) = 2^30.
  Taking the logarithm base 2 of both sides, we get n/2 = 30.
  Multiplying both sides by 2, we get n = 60.
  Therefore, the lake will be fully covered with lilies in 60 days.

Topic: Math
Question: A train M leaves City A at 5 am and reaches City B at 9am. Another train N leaves City B at 7am and reaches City A at 1030am. At what time do the 2 trains cross one another?
Choices:
  A: 1 hr 23 min
  B: 1 hr 15 min
  C: 1 hr 8 min
  D: 56 min
  E: 55 min
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Train M travels for 4 hours (5am to 9am) from City A to City B.
  Train N travels for 3.5 hours (7am to 10:30am) from City B to City A.
  The total distance traveled by both trains is the same.
  We can use the formula: time = distance / speed
  
Calculation:
  Let's assume the distance between City A and City B is "d".
  Let's assume the speed of Train M is "x" and the speed of Train N is "y".
  From the given information, we can write two equations:
  d = 4x   (since Train M travels for 4 hours)
  d = 3.5y + 2y  (since Train N travels for 3.5 hours after Train M has already traveled for 2 hours)
  Simplifying the second equation, we get:
  d = 5.5y
  Equating both equations, we get:
  4x = 5.5y
  x = (5.5/4)y
  Let's substitute this value of x in the first equation:
  d = 4x = 4(5.5/4)y = 5.5y
  So, the distance between City A and City B is 5.5y.
  Now, we can use the formula: time = distance / speed to find the time taken by each train to cover this distance.
  Time taken by Train M = (5.5y) / x = (5.5y) / (5.5/4)y = 4 hours
  Time taken by Train N = (5.5y) / y = 5.5 hours
  So, the two trains cross each other after 4 hours from 5am, which is at 9am.
  Therefore, the answer is 9am.

  speed of train N * (-2) = 0
  speed of train N = 0
  
  This is not possible, as the speed of train N cannot be zero.
  Therefore, the two trains do not cross each other.

  Distance travelled by Train N in x hours = speed of Train N * x

  t + (t - 2) = 5.5
  2t = 7.5

Topic: Math
Question: The average (arithmetic mean) of the weight of 10 vehicles is 12.2 tons. The average weight of the group of vehicles increased by 2.6 tons after a new heavy duty truck was added to the group? What is the weight in tons of the heavy duty truck?
Choices:
  A: 40.8
  B: 41.6
  C: 42.2
  D: 43.5
  E: 44.8
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The formula for the arithmetic mean is: sum of all values / number of values.
  Let's call the sum of the weights of the 10 vehicles "S" and the weight of the new heavy duty truck "x".
  We know that (S/10) = 12.2 and ((S+x)/11) = 14.8 (because the new average is 2.6 tons more than the original average).
  We can use these two equations to solve for x.
  Simplifying the second equation, we get S + x = 162.8.
  We can substitute the first equation into the second equation to get 10(12.2) + x = 162.8.
  Solving for x, we get x = 44.6.
Action: Answer("E")

Topic: Math
Question: 10kg of a mixture contains 30% sand and 70% clay. In order to make the mixture contain equal quantities of clay and sand how much of the mixture is to be removed and replaced with pure sand?
Choices:
  A: 10/7
  B: 20/7
  C: 30/7
  D: 40/7
  E: 50/7
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The initial mixture contains 30% sand and 70% clay.
  We want to remove and replace some of the mixture with pure sand to make the mixture contain equal quantities of clay and sand.
  Let's assume that we remove and replace x kg of the mixture.
  After removing and replacing x kg of the mixture, the amount of sand in the mixture will be 0.3(10 - x) + x = 0.3(10) + 0.7x = 3 + 0.7x.
  Similarly, the amount of clay in the mixture will be 0.7(10 - x) = 7 - 0.7x.
  We want the amount of sand to be equal to the amount of clay, so we can set up the equation: 3 + 0.7x = 7 - 0.7x.
  Solving for x, we get x = 2.

Topic: Math
Question: What will be the cost of gardening 1-metre – broad boundary around a rectangular plot having perimeter of 340 metres at the rate of 10 per square metre?
Choices:
  A: 3400
  B: 1700
  C: 3440
  D: Cannot be determined
  E: None of these
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  The perimeter of a rectangle is the sum of the lengths of all its sides.
  Let's assume that the length of the rectangular plot is L and the width is W.
  The perimeter of the rectangular plot is 2L + 2W = 340.
  We can simplify this to L + W = 170.
  The cost of gardening 1-meter broad boundary around the rectangular plot is the same as finding the area of the rectangular plot with dimensions (L+2) and (W+2) and then multiplying it by 10.
  The area of the rectangular plot is L * W.
  The area of the rectangular plot with the 1-meter broad boundary is (L+2) * (W+2).
  Therefore, the cost of gardening 1-meter broad boundary around the rectangular plot is 10 * [(L+2) * (W+2) - L * W].
Action: Answer("C") 
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Perimeter of a rectangle = 2(length + breadth)
  Here, perimeter = 340 meters
  Let the length of the rectangular plot be L and the breadth be B.
  We know that 2(L+B) = 340
  L+B = 170
  We need to find the cost of gardening 1-meter broad boundary around the rectangular plot.
  The area of the rectangular plot = L*B
  The area of the rectangular plot with a 1-meter broad boundary = (L+2)*(B+2)
  The area of the boundary = (L+2)*(B+2) - L*B
  The cost of gardening 1-meter broad boundary = 10 * area of the boundary

Calculation:
  L+B = 170
  B = 170 - L
  Area of the boundary = (L+2)*(B+2) - L*B
                       = (L+2)*(170-L+2) - L*(170-L)
                       = 344 - L^2
  Cost of gardening 1-meter broad boundary = 10 * area of the boundary
                                          = 10 * (344 - L^2)

Action: Answer("C")
Response 2:
Knowledge: 
  The perimeter of a rectangle is the sum of all its sides.
  Let's assume that the length of the rectangular plot is L and the width is W.
  The perimeter of the rectangular plot is 2(L+W).
  The cost of gardening 1-meter boundary around the rectangular plot is the cost of gardening the length and width of the rectangular plot plus the cost of gardening the four corners.
  The cost of gardening is given as 10 per square meter.
  The area of the rectangular plot is L*W.
  The area of the 1-meter boundary is (L+2)*(W+2) - L*W = 2L + 2W + 4.
  The cost of gardening the rectangular plot is 10*L*W.
  The cost of gardening the 1-meter boundary is 10*(2L + 2W + 4).
  We are given that the perimeter of the rectangular plot is 340 meters, so 2(L+W) = 340, which simplifies to L+W = 170.
Action: Answer("C")  
To find the cost of gardening the 1-meter boundary, we need to find the values of L and W. We know that L+W = 170, so we can solve for one variable in terms of the other. Let's solve for L:
L = 170 - W
Now we can substitute this value of L into the equation for the area of the 1-meter boundary:
Area of 1-meter boundary = (L+2)*(W+2) - L*W
= (170-W+2)*(W+2) - (170-W)*W
= 2W + 344
Finally, we can find the cost of gardening the 1-meter boundary by multiplying the area by the cost per square meter:
Cost of gardening 1-meter boundary = 10*(2W + 344)
= 20W + 3440
We don't know the value of W, but we can see that the only answer choice that matches this expression is C, so we can select that as our answer.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 1.0 | Problem 90 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Calculate the percentage gain of a merchant who purchased 90 kg of oranges for Rs. 450 and sold the whole lot at the rate of Rs. 7.50 per kg.
Choices:
  A: 50 %
  B: 60 %
  C: 55 %
  D: 70 %
  E: 58%
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Percentage gain is calculated as (Profit/Cost Price) * 100.
  Cost Price is the price at which the merchant purchased the oranges.
  Profit is the difference between the selling price and the cost price.
  Selling price is the price at which the merchant sold the oranges.
  The merchant purchased 90 kg of oranges for Rs. 450, so the cost price per kg is 450/90 = Rs. 5.
  The merchant sold the oranges at the rate of Rs. 7.50 per kg, so the selling price per kg is Rs. 7.50.
  Profit per kg = Selling price per kg - Cost price per kg = Rs. 7.50 - Rs. 5 = Rs. 2.50.
  Total profit = Profit per kg * Total quantity = Rs. 2.50 * 90 = Rs. 225.
  Percentage gain = (Profit/Cost Price) * 100 = (225/450) * 100 = 50%.

Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Percentage gain is calculated as (Profit/Cost Price) * 100
  Cost Price is the price at which the merchant purchased the oranges.
  Profit is the difference between the selling price and the cost price.
  Selling price is the price at which the merchant sold the oranges.
  The merchant purchased 90 kg of oranges for Rs. 450, so the cost price per kg is 450/90 = Rs. 5.
  The merchant sold the whole lot at the rate of Rs. 7.50 per kg, so the selling price per kg is Rs. 7.50.
  Profit = Selling Price - Cost Price = Rs. (7.50 - 5) * 90 = Rs. 225.
Action: Answer("B")  
Profit Percentage = (Profit/Cost Price) * 100 = (225/450) * 100 = 50%. 
Therefore, the percentage gain of the merchant is 50%, which is option B.

  D: 28 days

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 1.0 | Problem 93 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Joe's age, Joe's sister's age and Joe’s fathers age sums up to 100. When Joe is as old as his father, Joe's sister will be twice as old as now. When Joe is as old as his father then his father is twice as old as when his sister was as old as her father. Find the age of Joe's father?
Choices:
  A: 45
  B: 48
  C: 50
  D: 55
  E: 58
Response 0:
Let's start by assigning variables to the ages of Joe, his sister, and his father. Let J be Joe's age, S be his sister's age, and F be his father's age. 

From the first sentence, we know that:

J + S + F = 100

From the second sentence, we know that when Joe is as old as his father:

J + F = 2(S)

We can simplify this to:

J = 2S - F

From the third sentence, we know that when Joe is as old as his father, his father is twice as old as when his sister was as old as her father. Let's call the age when Joe's sister was as old as his father "x". At that time, Joe's father was F - x years old, and Joe's sister was S - x years old. So we have:

F - x = 2(S - x)

Simplifying this equation, we get:

2x = F - S

Now we have three equations with three variables:

J + S + F = 100
J + F = 2S
2x = F - S

We can solve for J and S in terms of F:

J = 2S - F
S = (F - 2x)/3

Substituting these expressions into the first equation, we get:

(2S - F) + S + F = 100

Simplifying, we get:

3S = 100

S = 33.33

Substituting this value of S into the equation for S in terms of F, we get:

33.33 = (F - 2x)/3

Multiplying both sides by 3, we get:

F - 2x = 100

Substituting this expression for F - 2x into the equation for 2x in terms of F, we get:

2(F - 2x) = F - S

Substituting the values we know, we get:

2(F - 2(50)) = F - 33.33

Simplifying, we get:

F = 58

So the answer is E: 58.
Response 1:
Let's start by assigning variables to the ages of Joe, his sister, and his father. Let J be Joe's age, S be his sister's age, and F be his father's age. 

From the first sentence, we know that:

J + S + F = 100

From the second sentence, we know that when Joe is as old as his father (i.e. F), his sister will be twice as old as she is now (i.e. 2S). We can set up an equation:

J + F = 2S

We can simplify this equation by substituting the first equation:

S = 100 - J - F
J + F = 2(100 - J - F)
J + F = 200 - 2J - 2F
3J + 3F = 200

From the third sentence, we know that when Joe is as old as his father (i.e. F), his father will be twice as old as his sister was when she was as old as her father (i.e. F). We can set up another equation:

F = 2(F - S)

Again, we can simplify this equation by substituting the first equation:

F = 2(F - (100 - J - F))
F = 2J - 100

Now we have two equations with two variables (J and F):

3J + 3F = 200
2J - F = 100

We can solve for J by multiplying the second equation by 3 and adding it to the first equation:

9J - 3F + 3J + 3F = 500
12J = 500
J = 41.67

We can round J to the nearest whole number since we're dealing with ages. J is approximately 42. 

Now we can solve for F using the second equation:

2(42) - F = 100
F = 16

Therefore, Joe's father is 16 years old. 

Action: Answer("E")
Response 2:
Let's start by assigning variables to the ages of Joe, his sister, and his father. Let J be Joe's age, S be his sister's age, and F be his father's age. 

From the first sentence, we know that:

J + S + F = 100

From the second sentence, we know that when Joe is as old as his father:

J + F = 2(S)

Simplifying this equation, we get:

J = 2S - F

From the third sentence, we know that when Joe is as old as his father, his father is twice as old as when his sister was as old as her father. Let's call the age of Joe's sister when she was as old as her father x. At that time, Joe's father was F - x years old. So, we can write:

J + F = 2(F - x)

Simplifying this equation, we get:

J = 2x - F

Now we have two expressions for J, so we can set them equal to each other:

2S - F = 2x - F

Simplifying this equation, we get:

S = x

So, we know that Joe's sister was x years old when her father was F - x years old, and we know that their ages sum up to 100:

J + S + F = 100

2x + F = 100

F = 100 - 2x

Now we can substitute this expression for F into the equation we got from the second sentence:

J + F = 2(S)

J + (100 - 2x) = 2x

J = 4x - 100

Finally, we can substitute this expression for J into the equation we got from the first sentence:

J + S + F = 100

(4x - 100) + x + (100 - 2x) = 100

3x = 100

x = 33.33 (repeating)

So, Joe's sister was 33.33 (repeating) years old when her father was twice as old as she was, which means Joe's father was 66.67 (repeating) years old at that time. 

Now we can use the expression we got for F in terms of x to find Joe's father's age:

F = 100 - 2x

F = 100 - 2(33.33)

F = 33.33

Action: Answer("E")
Response 3:
Let's start by assigning variables to the ages of Joe, his sister, and his father. Let J be Joe's age, S be his sister's age, and F be his father's age. 

From the first sentence, we know that:

J + S + F = 100

From the second sentence, we know that when Joe is as old as his father:

J + F = 2(S)

Simplifying this equation, we get:

J = 2S - F

From the third sentence, we know that when Joe is as old as his father, his father is twice as old as when his sister was as old as her father. Let's call the age of Joe's sister when she was as old as her father x. At that time, Joe's father was F - x years old. So, we have:

J + F = 2(F - x)

Simplifying this equation, we get:

J = 2x - F

Now we can set the two expressions for J equal to each other:

2S - F = 2x - F

Simplifying, we get:

2S = 2x

S = x

So, we know that Joe's sister was x years old when her father was F - x years old. We also know that the sum of their ages is 100:

J + S + F = 100

Substituting J = 2S - F and S = x, we get:

2x - F + x + F = 100

Simplifying, we get:

3x = 100

x = 33.33 (repeating)

Since x = S, we know that Joe's sister is 33.33 (repeating) years old now. 

Substituting x = 33.33 (repeating) into J = 2x - F, we get:

J = 2(33.33 (repeating)) - F

J = 66.67 (repeating) - F

Substituting J = 66.67 (repeating) - F into J + F = 2(S), we get:

(66.67 (repeating) - F) + F = 2(33.33 (repeating))

Simplifying, we get:

66.67 (repeating) + F = 66.67 (repeating)

F = 33.33 (repeating)

From the second sentence, we know that when Joe is as old as his father:

J + F = 2(S)

Simplifying this equation, we get:

J = 2S - F

From the third sentence, we know that when Joe is as old as his father, his father is twice as old as when his sister was as old as her father. Let's call the age of Joe's sister when she was as old as her father x. At that time, Joe's father was F - x years old. So, we have:

J + F = 2(F - x)

Simplifying this equation, we get:

J = 2x - F

Now we can set the two expressions for J equal to each other:

2S - F = 2x - F

Simplifying this equation, we get:

S = x

S + (F - x) = 100

Substituting S = x, we get:

x + (F - x) = 100

Simplifying this equation, we get:

F = 100

Let's start by assigning variables to the ages of Joe, his sister, and his father. Let J be Joe's age, S be his sister's age, and F be his father's age.

J + S + F = 100

From the second sentence, we know that when Joe is as old as his father (i.e. F), his sister will be twice her current age (i.e. 2S). We can set up an equation:

J + F = 2S

We can simplify this equation by using the first equation to solve for S:

S = 100 - J - F

J + F = 2(100 - J - F)

3J + 3F = 200

F = 2(F - (100 - J - F))

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 1.0 | Problem 94 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Christopher and Jonathan were having bets. They decide that a coin will be flipped twenty times and each time it turns heads, Christopher will give $2 to Jonathan and each time it turns out to be Tails, Jonathan will give 3$ to Christopher. After flipping for twenty times none of the both won or lost any amount.
How many times did the coin landed on Heads ?
Choices:
  A: 10
  B: 23
  C: 16
  D: 18
  E: 12
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Each time the coin lands on Heads, Christopher gives $2 to Jonathan.
  Each time the coin lands on Tails, Jonathan gives $3 to Christopher.
  After flipping the coin twenty times, neither of them won or lost any amount.
  Let's assume that the coin landed on Heads x times.
  Therefore, the coin landed on Tails (20-x) times.
  Christopher gave $2 to Jonathan x times.
  Jonathan gave $3 to Christopher (20-x) times.
  The total amount given by Christopher to Jonathan is $2x.
  The total amount given by Jonathan to Christopher is $3(20-x) = $60 - $3x.
  The total amount given by Jonathan to Christopher is equal to the total amount given by Christopher to Jonathan.
  Therefore, 2x = 60 - 3x.
  Solving for x, we get x = 12.
Action: Answer("E")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Each time the coin lands on Heads, Christopher gives $2 to Jonathan.
  Each time the coin lands on Tails, Jonathan gives $3 to Christopher.
  After 20 flips, neither Christopher nor Jonathan won or lost any money.
  Let's assume that the coin landed on Heads x times and Tails y times.
  Therefore, Christopher gave 2x dollars to Jonathan and Jonathan gave 3y dollars to Christopher.
  Since neither of them won or lost any money, we can set up the following equation: 2x = 3y
  We also know that x + y = 20 (since there were 20 flips in total).
  We can use these two equations to solve for x (the number of times the coin landed on Heads).
  Solving for y in the second equation, we get y = 20 - x.
  Substituting this into the first equation, we get 2x = 3(20 - x).
  Simplifying this, we get 2x = 60 - 3x.
  Solving for x, we get x = 15.
Action: Answer("A")

  Simplifying, we get (5/3)x = 20, which gives us x = 12.

  Since the net amount won or lost by both is zero, we have:
  5x - 60 = -(40 - 5x)
  Solving for x, we get x = 12.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 1.0 | Problem 95 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Kevin drove from A to B at a constant speed of 70 mph. Once he reached B, he turned right around with pause, and returned to A at a constant speed of 90 mph. Exactly 3 hours before the end of his trip, he was still approaching B, only 70 miles away from it. What is the distance between A and B?
Choices:
  A: 180
  B: 90
  C: 270
  D: 360
  E: None of the above
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  - Distance = Speed x Time
  - Let's call the distance between A and B "d"
  - Let's call the time it takes Kevin to drive from A to B "t1"
  - Let's call the time it takes Kevin to drive from B to A "t2"
  - We know that t2 = t1 - 3 (since he has 3 hours left in his trip when he is 70 miles away from B)
  - We also know that d = 70t1 (since he drove at 70 mph for t1 hours to get from A to B) and d = 90t2 (since he drove at 90 mph for t2 hours to get from B to A)
Action: 
  - We can use the two equations above to solve for t1 and t2:
    - d = 70t1
    - d = 90(t1 - 3)
    - 70t1 = 90t1 - 270
    - 20t1 = 270
    - t1 = 13.5
    - t2 = t1 - 3 = 10.5
  - Now we can use either equation to solve for d:
    - d = 70t1 = 70(13.5) = 945
Action: Answer("E") None of the above. 
The distance between A and B is 945 miles, which is not one of the available choices.

  - We can substitute this value of t1 into the third equation:
    - t1 + t2 - 3 = (d - 70) / 90
    - (9/7)t2 + t2 - 3 = (d - 70) / 90
    - (16/7)t2 = (d + 200) / 90
    - t2 = (7/16)(d + 200) / 90
  - We can substitute this value of t2 into the equation for t1:
    - t1 = (9/7)t2
    - t1 = (9/7)(7/16)(d + 200) / 90
    - t1 = (9/16)(d + 200) / 90
  - We can substitute these values of t1 and t2 into the equation for d:
    - d = 70t1
    - d = 70[(9/16)(d + 200) / 90]
    - d = (63/8)(d + 200) / 9
    - 81d = 567d + 113400
    - 486d = 113400
    - d = 233.33 (rounded to the nearest hundredth)
  - The distance between A and B is approximately 233.33 miles.
Answer: Answer("E")
Response 9:
Knowledge:
  - Distance = Speed x Time
  - Let d be the distance between A and B
  - Let t1 be the time it takes Kevin to drive from A to B
  - Let t2 be the time it takes Kevin to drive from B to A
  - We know that t2 = t1 - 3 (since he has 3 hours left in his trip when he is 70 miles away from B)
  - We also know that d = 70t1 (since he is driving at 70 mph on the first leg of his trip)
  - And d = 90t2 (since he is driving at 90 mph on the second leg of his trip)
Action: 
  - We can substitute t2 = t1 - 3 into the second equation to get d = 90(t1 - 3)
  - Setting the two expressions for d equal to each other, we get 70t1 = 90(t1 - 3)
  - Solving for t1, we get t1 = 27
  - Substituting t1 into either equation for d, we get d = 70t1 = 1890
  - Therefore, the distance between A and B is 1890 miles.
  Answer: Answer("E")

Choices:

  With a 1 before it, the number becomes "1abcde".

  abcde1 = 3 * 1abcde
  100000a + 10000b + 1000c + 100d + 10e + 1 = 300000 + 30000a + 3000b + 300c + 30d + 3e
  70000a + 2000b + 200c - 29d - 2e = 299999

  B: 32456 does not satisfy the property of the number.
  C: 76523 does not satisfy the property of the number.
  D: 24567 satisfies the property of the number.
  E: 43566 does not satisfy the property of the number.

Response 1:
Knowledge:
  To solve this problem, we need to use algebraic equations.
  Let's assume the 5 digit number is "abcde".
  According to the problem, if we add a 1 after it, the new number becomes "abcde1" and it is three times as large as it would be with a 1 before it, which is "1abcde".
  We can write this as an equation: 3(1abcde) = abcde1
  Simplifying this equation, we get: 299997a + 29997b + 2997c + 297d + 30e = 10a + b + c + d + e + 3
  Rearranging the terms, we get: 299987a + 29996b + 2967c + 267d = 27e + 3
  Since the left-hand side is divisible by 3, the right-hand side must also be divisible by 3. Therefore, e must be either 0 or 3.
  If e = 0, then the right-hand side is 3, which is not divisible by 27. Therefore, e must be 3.
  Substituting e = 3 into the equation, we get: 299987a + 29996b + 2967c + 267d = 84
  Since the left-hand side is divisible by 3, the right-hand side must also be divisible by 3. Therefore, d must be either 0 or 3 or 6 or 9.
  If d = 0, then the left-hand side is less than 84, which is a contradiction. Therefore, d must be either 3 or 6 or 9.
  Substituting d = 3 into the equation, we get: 299987a + 29996b + 2967c = 57
  Since the left-hand side is divisible by 3, the right-hand side must also be divisible by 3. Therefore, c must be either 0 or 3 or 6 or 9.
  If c = 0, then the left-hand side is less than 57, which is a contradiction. Therefore, c must be either 3 or 6 or 9.
  Substituting c = 3 into the equation, we get: 299987a + 29996b = 6
  Since the left-hand side is divisible by 2, the right-hand side must also be divisible by 2. Therefore, b must be even.
  If b = 0, then the left-hand side is less than 6, which is a contradiction. Therefore, b must be either 2 or 4 or 6 or 8.
  Substituting b = 2 into the equation, we get: 299987a = -58

    1bcde1 = 3 * 1bcde
    10001 * b + 1001 * c + 101 * d + 11 * e = 3 * (1000 * b + 100 * c + 10 * d + e)

    7 * e = -969 * b - 91 * c
    e = -139 * b - 13 * c

  Therefore, e = -139 * 4 - 13 * 2 = -564, which means that e = 6.
  Substituting a = 1, b = 4, c = 2, and e = 6 into the original number abcde, we get:
    abcde = 14206
